title="Dorset culture">Dorset settlement</a></span> </div></th><td>8th century BC</td></tr><tr class="mergedrow"><th scope="row"><div style="text-indent:-0.9em;margin-left:1.2em;font-weight:normal;">&#8226;&#160;<span class="nowrap"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Norse_settlements_in_Greenland" title="Norse settlements in Greenland">Norse colonization</a></span> </div></th><td>10th century</td></tr><tr class="mergedrow"><th scope="row"><div style="text-indent:-0.9em;margin-left:1.2em;font-weight:normal;">&#8226;&#160;<span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Inuit" title="Inuit">Arrival of the Inuit</a></span> </div></th><td>13th century</td></tr><tr class="mergedrow"><th scope="row"><div style="text-indent:-0.9em;margin-left:1.2em;font-weight:normal;">&#8226;&#160;<span class="nowrap"><a </div></th><td>1262</td></tr><tr class="mergedrow"><th scope="row"><div style="text-indent:-0.9em;margin-left:1.2em;font-weight:normal;">&#8226;&#160;<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dano-Norwegian_empire" title="Dano-Norwegian empire">Dano-Norwegian colonies established</a> </div></th><td>1721</td></tr><tr class="mergedrow"><th scope="row"><div style="text-indent:-0.9em;margin-left:1.2em;font-weight:normal;">&#8226;&#160;<a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Kiel" title="Treaty of Kiel">Ceded to Denmark</a><sup class="reference" id="ref_ccc"><a href="#endnote_ccc">[c]</a></sup> </div></th><td>14 January 1814</td></tr><tr class="mergedrow"><th scope="row"><div style="text-indent:-0.9em;margin-left:1.2em;font-weight:normal;">&#8226;&#160;<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amt_(administrative_division)" title="Amt (administrative division)">Amt</a> status </div></th><td>5 June 1953</td></tr><tr class="mergedrow"><th scope="row"><div style="text-indent:-0.9em;margin-left:1.2em;font-weight:normal;">&#8226;&#160;Further autonomy and self rule </div></th><td>21 June 2009<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-selvstyre_4-0"><a href="/wiki/ISO_3166-2:GL" title="ISO 3166-2:GL">GL</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Country_code_top-level_domain" title="Country code top-level domain">Internet TLD</a></th><td><a href="/wiki/.gl" title=".gl">.gl</a></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><div style="text-align:left;margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;"><ol style="list-style-type: lower-alpha; margin-left: 1em; font-size:90%;">\n<li value="1"><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_aaa"><b><a href="#ref_aaa">^</a></b></span>  Greenlandic has been the sole official language of Greenland since 2009.<big><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-selvstyre_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-selvstyre-4">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-law_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-law-9">[8]</a></sup></big></li><li value="2"><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_bbb"><b><a href="#ref_bbb">^</a></b></span>  Danish influence reached Greenland in 1380 with the reign of <a href="/wiki/Olaf_II_of_Denmark" title="Olaf II of Denmark">Olav IV</a> in Norway, son of <a href="/wiki/Haakon_VI_of_Norway" title="Haakon VI of Norway">Haakon VI of Norway</a> and <a href="/wiki/Margaret_I_of_Denmark" title="Margaret I of Denmark">Margaret I of Denmark</a>.</li><li value="3"><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_ccc"><b><a href="#ref_ccc">^</a></b></span>  Although previously under Danish monarchy for four hundred years, Greenland, the <a href="/wiki/Faroe_Islands" title="Faroe Islands">Faroe Islands</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Iceland" title="Iceland">Iceland</a> were formally Norwegian possessions until 1814.</li><li value="4"><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_ddd"><b><a href="#ref_ddd">^</a></b></span> As of 2000:<br/>410,449&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (158,475&#160;sq&#160;mi) ice-free;<br/>1,755,637&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (677,855&#160;sq&#160;mi) ice-covered.<br/>Density: 0.14/km<sup>2</sup> (0.36 /sq.&#160;mi) for ice-free areas.</li>\n</ol></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Greenland</b> (<a href="/wiki/Greenlandic_language" title="Greenlandic language">Greenlandic</a>: <i lang="kl">Kalaallit Nunaat</i>, <small>pronounced&#160;</small><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[kala&#720;&#620;it nuna&#720;t]</a></span>; <a href="/wiki/Danish_language" title="Danish language">Danish</a>: <i lang="da">Gr&#248;nland</i>, <small>pronounced&#160;</small><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Danish" title="Help:IPA/Danish">[&#712;&#609;&#641;&#630;n&#716;lan&#704;]</a></span>) is an autonomous <a href="/wiki/Denmark#Greenland_and_the_Faroe_Islands" title="Denmark">constituent country</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">Kingdom of Denmark</a> between the <a href="/wiki/Arctic_Ocean" title="Arctic Ocean">Arctic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic</a> oceans, east of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canadian_Arctic_Archipelago" title="Canadian Arctic Archipelago">Canadian Arctic Archipelago</a>. Though <a href="/wiki/Physical_geography" title="Physical geography">physiographically</a> a part of the continent of <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a>, Greenland has been politically and culturally associated with Europe (specifically <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a> and Denmark, the <a href="/wiki/Colonialism" title="Colonialism">colonial powers</a>, as well as the nearby island of <a href="/wiki/Iceland" title="Iceland">Iceland</a>) for more than a millennium.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brown2000_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-Brown2000-10">[9]</a></sup> The majority of its residents are <a href="/wiki/Inuit" title="Inuit">Inuit</a>, whose ancestors began migrating from the Canadian mainland in the 13th century, gradually settling across the island.\n</p><p>Greenland is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_islands_by_area" title="List of islands by area">world\'s largest island</a>. <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Antarctica" title="Antarctica">Antarctica</a> (both larger) are generally considered to be continental landmasses rather than islands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jc_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-jc-11">[10]</a></sup>  Three-quarters of Greenland is covered by the only permanent <a href="/wiki/Greenland_ice_sheet" title="Greenland ice sheet">ice sheet</a> outside <a href="/wiki/Antarctica" title="Antarctica">Antarctica</a>. With a population of about 56,480 (2013),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Greenland_in_Figures_2013_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-Greenland_in_Figures_2013-7">[6]</a></sup> it is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_and_dependencies_by_population_density" title="List of countries and dependencies by population density">least densely populated territory</a> in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-popden_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-popden-12">[11]</a></sup> About a third of the population live in <a href="/wiki/Nuuk" title="Nuuk">Nuuk</a>, the capital and largest city. The <a href="/wiki/Arctic_Umiaq_Line" title="Arctic Umiaq Line">Arctic Umiaq Line</a> ferry acts as a lifeline for western Greenland, connecting the various cities and settlements.\n</p><p>Greenland has been inhabited at intervals over at least the last 4,500 years by Arctic peoples whose forebears migrated there from what is now <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-natmus_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-natmus-13">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[13]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Vikings" title="Vikings">Norsemen</a> settled the uninhabited southern part of Greenland beginning in the 10th century, having previously settled <a href="/wiki/Iceland" title="Iceland">Iceland</a> to escape persecution from the <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Norway" title="Monarchy of Norway">King of Norway</a> and his central government. These Norsemen would later set sail from Greenland and Iceland, with <a href="/wiki/Leif_Erikson" title="Leif Erikson">Leif Erikson</a> becoming the first known European to reach North America nearly 500 years before <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">Columbus</a> reached the Caribbean islands. <a href="/wiki/Inuit" title="Inuit">Inuit</a> peoples arrived in the 13th century. Though under continuous influence of <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a> and Norwegians, Greenland was not formally under the Norwegian crown until 1262. The Norse colonies disappeared in the late 15th&#160;century when Norway was hit by the <a href="/wiki/Black_Death" title="Black Death">Black Death</a> and entered a severe decline. Soon after their demise, beginning in 1499, the Portuguese briefly explored and claimed the island, naming it <i>Terra do Lavrador</i> (later applied to <a href="/wiki/Labrador" title="Labrador">Labrador</a> in Canada).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[14]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the early 18th century, Danish explorers reached Greenland again. To strengthen trading and power, <a href="/wiki/Denmark%E2%80%93Norway" title="Denmark&#8211;Norway">Denmark&#8211;Norway</a> affirmed sovereignty over the island. Because of Norway\'s weak status, it lost sovereignty over Greenland in 1814 when the union was dissolved. Greenland became Danish in 1814, and was fully integrated in the Danish state in 1953 under the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Denmark" title="Constitution of Denmark">Constitution of Denmark</a>.\n</p><p>In 1973, Greenland joined the <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Community" title="European Economic Community">European Economic Community</a> with Denmark. However, in a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greenlandic_European_Economic_Community_membership_referendum,_1982" title="Greenlandic European Economic Community membership referendum, 1982">referendum</a> in 1982, a majority of the population voted for Greenland to withdraw from the <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Community" title="European Economic Community">EEC</a>, which was effected in 1985. Greenland contains the world\'s largest and most northerly <a href="/wiki/National_park" title="National park">national park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Northeast_Greenland_National_Park" title="Northeast Greenland National Park">Northeast Greenland National Park</a> (<i>Kalaallit Nunaanni nuna eqqissisimatitaq</i>). Established in 1974, and expanded to its present size in 1988, it protects 972,001 square kilometres (375,292&#160;sq&#160;mi) of the interior and northeastern coast of Greenland and is bigger than all but twenty-nine countries in the world. Greenland is divided into five <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_Greenland" title="Administrative divisions of Greenland">municipalities</a> &#8211; <a href="/wiki/Sermersooq" title="Sermersooq">Sermersooq</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kujalleq" title="Kujalleq">Kujalleq</a>, <a href="/wiki/Qeqertalik" title="Qeqertalik">Qeqertalik</a>, <a href="/wiki/Qeqqata" title="Qeqqata">Qeqqata</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Avannaata" title="Avannaata">Avannaata</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Qaasuitsoq2018_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-Qaasuitsoq2018-16">[15]</a></sup> Greenland does not have an independent seat at the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[16]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greenlandic_home_rule_referendum,_1979" title="Greenlandic home rule referendum, 1979">1979</a>, Denmark granted <a href="/wiki/Home_rule" title="Home rule">home rule</a> to Greenland, and in 2008, Greenlanders <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greenlandic_self-government_referendum,_2008" title="Greenlandic self-government referendum, 2008">voted</a> in favor of the Self-Government Act, which transferred more power from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Government_of_Denmark" title="Government of Denmark">Danish government</a> to the local <a href="/wiki/Naalakkersuisut" title="Naalakkersuisut">Greenlandic government</a>. Under the new structure, in effect since 21 June 2009,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Greenland_In_Figures_2012_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-Greenland_In_Figures_2012-18">[17]</a></sup> Greenland can gradually assume responsibility for policing, judicial system, company law, accounting, and auditing; mineral resource activities; aviation; law of legal capacity, family law and succession law; aliens and border controls; the working environment; and <a href="/wiki/Financial_regulation" title="Financial regulation">financial regulation</a> and supervision, while the Danish government retains control of foreign affairs and defence. It also retains control of monetary policy, providing an initial annual subsidy of <a href="/wiki/Danish_krone" title="Danish krone">DKK</a> 3.4&#160;billion, which is planned to diminish gradually over time. Greenland expects to grow its economy based on increased income from the extraction of natural resources. The capital, <a href="/wiki/Nuuk" title="Nuuk">Nuuk</a>, held the <a href="/wiki/2016_Arctic_Winter_Games" title="2016 Arctic Winter Games">2016 Arctic Winter Games</a>. At 70%, Greenland has one of the highest shares of renewable energy in the world, mostly coming from hydropower.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[18]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs additional references to reliable sources. (March 2017)">additional citation(s) needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p>\n<div class="toc" id="toc"><input class="toctogglecheckbox" id="toctogglecheckbox" role="button" style="display:none"
