class="toclevel-2 tocsection-29"><a href="#Works_cited"><span class="tocnumber">11.2</span> <span class="toctext">Works cited</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-30"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-31"><a href="#Overviews_and_data"><span class="tocnumber">12.1</span> <span class="toctext">Overviews and data</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-32"><a href="#Government_2"><span class="tocnumber">12.2</span> <span class="toctext">Government</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-33"><a href="#Trade"><span class="tocnumber">12.3</span> <span class="toctext">Trade</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-34"><a href="#Travel"><span class="tocnumber">12.4</span> <span class="toctext">Travel</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-35"><a href="#Other"><span class="tocnumber">12.5</span> <span class="toctext">Other</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span></h2>\n<p>The early Norse settlers named the island as <i>Greenland.</i> In the <a href="/wiki/Sagas_of_Icelanders" title="Sagas of Icelanders">Icelandic sagas</a>, the Norwegian-born Icelander <a href="/wiki/Erik_the_Red" title="Erik the Red">Erik the Red</a> was said to be exiled from <a href="/wiki/Iceland" title="Iceland">Iceland</a> for manslaughter. Along with his extended family and his <a href="/wiki/Thrall" title="Thrall">thralls</a> (i.e. slaves or serfs), he set out in ships to explore an icy land known to lie to the northwest. After finding a habitable area and settling there, he named it <i><i lang="non" title="Old Norse language text"><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/Gr%C5%93nland" title="wikt:Gr&#339;nland">Gr&#339;nland</a></i></i> (translated as "Greenland"), supposedly in the hope that the pleasant name would attract settlers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ancientstandard_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-ancientstandard-21">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Grove_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-Grove-22">[21]</a></sup>  The <i><a href="/wiki/Saga_of_Erik_the_Red" title="Saga of Erik the Red">Saga of Erik the Red</a></i> states: "In the summer, Erik left to settle in the country he had found, which he called Greenland, as he said people would be attracted there if it had a favorable name."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[22]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The name of the country in the indigenous <a href="/wiki/Greenlandic_language" title="Greenlandic language">Greenlandic language</a> is <i lang="kl" title="Greenlandic language text">Kalaallit Nunaat</i> ("land of the Kalaallit").<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-InuitDictionary_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-InuitDictionary-24">[23]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Kalaallit" title="Kalaallit">Kalaallit</a> are the <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples" title="Indigenous peoples">indigenous</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greenlandic_Inuit_people" title="Greenlandic Inuit people">Greenlandic Inuit people</a> who inhabit the country\'s western region.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Greenland" title="History of Greenland">History of Greenland</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_Paleo-Eskimo_cultures">Early Paleo-Eskimo cultures</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Arctic_cultures_900-1500.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="989" data-file-width="259" decoding="async" height="649" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Arctic_cultures_900-1500.png/170px-Arctic_cultures_900-1500.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Arctic_cultures_900-1500.png/255px-Arctic_cultures_900-1500.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/32/Arctic_cultures_900-1500.png 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Arctic_cultures_900-1500.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Maps showing the different cultures in Greenland, Labrador, Newfoundland and the Canadian arctic islands in the years 900, 1100, 1300 and 1500. Green: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dorset_Culture" title="Dorset Culture">Dorset Culture</a>; blue: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thule_Culture" title="Thule Culture">Thule Culture</a>; red: <a href="/wiki/Norsemen" title="Norsemen">Norse culture</a>; yellow: <a href="/wiki/Innu" title="Innu">Innu</a>; orange: <a href="/wiki/Beothuk" title="Beothuk">Beothuk</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>In <a href="/wiki/Prehistory" title="Prehistory">prehistoric times</a>, Greenland was home to several successive <a href="/wiki/Paleo-Eskimo" title="Paleo-Eskimo">Paleo-Eskimo</a> cultures known today primarily through archaeological finds. The earliest entry of the Paleo-Eskimo into Greenland is thought to have occurred about 2500&#160;BC. From around 2500&#160;BC to 800&#160;BC, southern and western Greenland were inhabited by the <a href="/wiki/Saqqaq_culture" title="Saqqaq culture">Saqqaq culture</a>. Most finds of Saqqaq-period archaeological remains have been around <a href="/wiki/Disko_Bay" title="Disko Bay">Disko Bay</a>, including the site of Saqqaq, after which the culture is named.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[25]</a></sup>\n</p><p>From 2400&#160;BC to 1300&#160;BC, the <a href="/wiki/Independence_I_culture" title="Independence I culture">Independence I culture</a> existed in northern Greenland. It was a part of the <a href="/wiki/Arctic_small_tool_tradition" title="Arctic small tool tradition">Arctic small tool tradition</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Greenland_History_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-Greenland_History-27">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Greenland_Migration_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-Greenland_Migration-28">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[28]</a></sup> Towns, including <a href="/wiki/Deltaterrasserne" title="Deltaterrasserne">Deltaterrasserne</a>, started to appear.\n</p><p>Around 800&#160;BC, the Saqqaq culture disappeared and the Early <a href="/wiki/Dorset_culture" title="Dorset culture">Dorset culture</a> emerged in western Greenland and the <a href="/wiki/Independence_II_culture" title="Independence II culture">Independence II culture</a> in northern Greenland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[29]</a></sup> The Dorset culture was the first culture to extend throughout the Greenlandic coastal areas, both on the west and east coasts. It lasted until the total onset of the <a href="/wiki/Thule_people" title="Thule people">Thule culture</a> in 1500&#160;AD. The Dorset culture population lived primarily from hunting of <a href="/wiki/Aboriginal_whaling" title="Aboriginal whaling">whales</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caribou" title="Caribou">caribou</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[31]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[33]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Norse_settlement">Norse settlement</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Herjolfsnes_(Norse_Greenland)" title="Herjolfsnes (Norse Greenland)">Herjolfsnes (Norse Greenland)</a></div>\n<p>From 986, Greenland\'s west coast was settled by <a href="/wiki/Icelanders" title="Icelanders">Icelanders</a> and <a href="/wiki/Norwegians" title="Norwegians">Norwegians</a>, through a contingent of 14 boats led by <a href="/wiki/Erik_the_Red" title="Erik the Red">Erik the Red</a>. They formed three settlements&#8212;known as the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Settlement" title="Eastern Settlement">Eastern Settlement</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Western_Settlement" title="Western Settlement">Western Settlement</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Ivittuut" title="Ivittuut">Middle Settlement</a>&#8212;on <a href="/wiki/Fjord" title="Fjord">fjords</a> near the southwestern-most tip of the island.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brown2000_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-Brown2000-10">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[34]</a></sup> They shared the island with the late <a href="/wiki/Dorset_culture" title="Dorset culture">Dorset culture</a> inhabitants who occupied the northern and western parts, and later with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thule_culture" title="Thule culture">Thule culture</a> that entered from the north. Norse Greenlanders submitted to Norwegian rule in 1261 under the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Norway_(872%E2%80%931397)" title="Kingdom of Norway (872&#8211;1397)">Kingdom of Norway (872&#8211;1397)</a>. Later the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Norway" title="Kingdom of Norway">Kingdom of Norway</a> entered into a personal union with Denmark in 1380, and from 1397 was a part of the <a href="/wiki/Kalmar_Union" title="Kalmar Union">Kalmar Union</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[35]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gron-rune-kingigtorssuaq.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="316" data-file-width="896" decoding="async" height="60" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Gron-rune-kingigtorssuaq.jpg/170px-Gron-rune-kingigtorssuaq.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Gron-rune-kingigtorssuaq.jpg/255px-Gron-rune-kingigtorssuaq.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Gron-rune-kingigtorssuaq.jpg/340px-Gron-rune-kingigtorssuaq.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gron-rune-kingigtorssuaq.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Kingittorsuaq_Runestone" title="Kingittorsuaq Runestone">Kingittorsuaq Runestone</a> from <a href="/wiki/Kingittorsuaq_Island" title="Kingittorsuaq Island">Kingittorsuaq Island</a> (<a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a>)</div></div></div>\n<p>Erik the Red\'s recruitment of others to settle in Greenland has been characterized recently as a land scam, the scam (and the name) portraying Greenland as better farm land than in Iceland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[36]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Norse settlements, such as <a href="/wiki/Brattahl%C3%AD%C3%B0" title="Brattahl&#237;&#240;">Brattahl&#237;&#240;</a>, thrived for centuries but disappeared sometime in the 15th century, perhaps at the onset of the <a href="/wiki/Little_Ice_Age" title="Little Ice Age">Little Ice Age</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Diamond_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-Diamond-38">[37]</a></sup> Apart from some <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Runic" title="Runic">runic</a> inscriptions, no contemporary records or <a href="/wiki/Historiography" title="Historiography">historiography</a> survives from the Norse settlements. Medieval Norwegian sagas and historical works mention Greenland\'s economy as well as the bishops of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gardar_(see)" title="Gardar (see)">Gardar</a> and the collection of tithes. A chapter in the <i><a href="/wiki/Konungs_skuggsj%C3%A1" title="Konungs skuggsj&#225;">Konungs skuggsj&#225;</a></i> (The King\'s Mirror) describes Norse Greenland\'s exports and imports as well as grain cultivation.\n</p><p>Icelandic saga accounts of life in Greenland were composed in the 13th century and later, and do not constitute primary sources for the history of early Norse Greenland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Grove_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-Grove-22">[21]</a></sup> Modern understanding therefore mostly depends on the physical data from archeological sites. Interpretation of <a href="/wiki/Ice_core" title="Ice core">ice core</a> and <a href="/wiki/Clam" title="Clam">clam</a> shell data suggests that between 800 and 1300, the regions around the fjords of southern Greenland experienced a relatively mild climate several degrees Celsius higher than usual in the North Atlantic,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Arnold_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-Arnold-39">[38]</a></sup> with trees and <a href="/wiki/Herbaceous_plant" title="Herbaceous plant">herbaceous plants</a> growing, and livestock being farmed. <a href="/wiki/Barley" title="Barley">Barley</a> was grown as a crop up to the 70th&#160;parallel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[39]</a></sup> What is verifiable is that the ice cores indicate Greenland has had dramatic temperature shifts many times over the past 100,000 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[40]</a></sup> Similarly the <a href="/wiki/Landn%C3%A1mab%C3%B3k" title="Landn&#225;mab&#243;k">Icelandic Book of Settlements</a> records <a href="/wiki/Famine" title="Famine">famines</a> during the winters, in which "the old and helpless were killed and thrown over cliffs".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Arnold_39-1"><a href="#cite_note-Arnold-39">[38]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hvalsey_Church.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2736" data-file-width="3648" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Hvalsey_Church.jpg/220px-Hvalsey_Church.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Hvalsey_Church.jpg/330px-Hvalsey_Church.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Hvalsey_Church.jpg/440px-Hvalsey_Church.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hvalsey_Church.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>One of the last contemporary written mentions of the <a href="/wiki/Norsemen" title="Norsemen">Norse</a> Greenlanders records a marriage which took place in 1408 in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Church_of_Hvalsey" title="Church of Hvalsey">church of Hvalsey</a>&#8212;today the best-preserved Nordic ruins in Greenland.</div></div></div>\n<p>These <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Norse_colonization_of_Greenland" title="Norse colonization of Greenland">Icelandic settlements</a> vanished during the 14th and early 15th&#160;centuries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[41]</a></sup> The demise of the Western Settlement coincides with a decrease in summer and winter temperatures. A study of North Atlantic seasonal temperature variability during the <a href="/wiki/Little_Ice_Age" title="Little Ice Age">Little Ice Age</a> showed a significant decrease in maximum summer temperatures beginning in the late 13th century to early 14th century&#8212;as much as 6 to 8&#160;&#176;C (11 to 14&#160;&#176;F) lower than modern summer temperatures.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[42]</a></sup> The study also found that the lowest winter temperatures of the last 2000 years occurred in the late 14th century and early 15th century. The Eastern Settlement was likely abandoned in the early to mid-15th century, during this cold period.\n</p><p>Theories drawn from archeological excavations at <a href="/wiki/Herjolfsnes" title="Herjolfsnes">Herjolfsnes</a> in the 1920s, suggest that the condition of human bones from this period indicates that the Norse population was <a href="/wiki/Malnutrition" title="Malnutrition">malnourished</a>, maybe due to <a href="/wiki/Erosion" title="Erosion">soil erosion</a> resulting from the Norsemen\'s destruction of natural vegetation in the course of farming, turf-cutting, and wood-cutting. Malnutrition may also have resulted from widespread deaths due to <a href="/wiki/Pandemic" title="Pandemic">pandemic</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Infectious_disease" title="Infectious disease">plague</a>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IngstadIngstad2000_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-IngstadIngstad2000-44">[43]</a></sup> the decline in temperatures during the Little Ice Age; and armed conflicts with the <i><a href="/wiki/Skr%C3%A6ling" title="Skr&#230;ling">Skr&#230;lings</a></i> (Norse word for Inuit, meaning "wretches"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Diamond_38-1"><a href="#cite_note-Diamond-38">[37]</a></sup>). In 1379, the Inuit attacked the Eastern Settlement, killed 18 men and captured two boys and a woman.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Diamond_38-2"><a href="#cite_note-Diamond-38">[37]</a></sup> Recent archeological studies somewhat challenge the general assumption that the Norse colonisation had a dramatic negative environmental effect on the vegetation. Data support traces of a possible Norse soil amendment strategy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[44]</a></sup> More recent evidence suggests that the Norse, who never numbered more than about 2,500, gradually abandoned the Greenland settlements over the 1400s as <a href="/wiki/Walrus_ivory" title="Walrus ivory">walrus ivory</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LeoneKnauf2015_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-LeoneKnauf2015-46">[45]</a></sup> the most valuable export from Greenland, decreased in price due to competition with other sources of higher-quality ivory, and that there was actually little evidence of starvation or difficulties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[46]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Other theories about the disappearance of the Norse settlement have been proposed;\n</p>\n<ol><li>Lack of support from the homeland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IngstadIngstad2000_44-1"><a href="#cite_note-IngstadIngstad2000-44">[43]</a></sup></li>\n<li>Ship-borne marauders (such as <a href="/wiki/Basques" title="Basques">Basque</a>, English, or German pirates) rather than <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Skraelings" title="Skraelings">Skraelings</a>, could have plundered and displaced the Greenlanders.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TriggerWashburn1996_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-TriggerWashburn1996-48">[47]</a></sup></li>\n<li>They were "the victims of hidebound thinking and of a hierarchical society dominated by the Church and the biggest land owners. In their reluctance to see themselves as anything but Europeans, the Greenlanders failed to adopt the kind of apparel that the Inuit employed as protection against the cold and damp or to borrow any of the Eskimo hunting gear."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brown2000_10-2"><a href="#cite_note-Brown2000-10">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Diamond_38-3"><a href="#cite_note-Diamond-38">[37]</a></sup></li>\n<li>"Norse society\'s structure created a conflict between the short-term interests of those in power, and the long-term interests of the society as a whole."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Diamond_38-4"><a href="#cite_note-Diamond-38">[37]</a></sup></li></ol>\n<h3><span id="Thule_culture_.281300.E2.80.93present.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Thule_culture_(1300&#8211;present)">Thule culture (1300&#8211;present)</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Billeder_fra_Gr%C3%B8nland_11441.tif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4254" data-file-width="5512" decoding="async" height="170" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Billeder_fra_Gr%C3%B8nland_11441.tif/lossy-page1-220px-Billeder_fra_Gr%C3%B8nland_11441.tif.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Billeder_fra_Gr%C3%B8nland_11441.tif/lossy-page1-330px-Billeder_fra_Gr%C3%B8nland_11441.tif.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Billeder_fra_Gr%C3%B8nland_11441.tif/lossy-page1-440px-Billeder_fra_Gr%C3%B8nland_11441.tif.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Billeder_fra_Gr%C3%B8nland_11441.tif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Pictures of Greenland, c. 1863</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Thule_people" title="Thule people">Thule people</a> are the ancestors of the current Greenlandic population. No genes from the Paleo-Eskimos have been found in the present population of Greenland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[48]</a></sup> The Thule Culture migrated eastward from what is now known as <a href="/wiki/Alaska" title="Alaska">Alaska</a> around 1000, reaching Greenland around 1300. The Thule culture was the first to introduce to Greenland such technological innovations as <a href="/wiki/Dog_sled" title="Dog sled">dog sleds</a> and <a href="/wiki/Toggling_harpoon" title="Toggling harpoon">toggling harpoons</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="1500.E2.80.931814"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1500&#8211;1814">1500&#8211;1814</span></h3>\n<p>In 1500, King <a href="/wiki/Manuel_I_of_Portugal" title="Manuel I of Portugal">Manuel&#160;I of Portugal</a> sent <a href="/wiki/Gaspar_Corte-Real" title="Gaspar Corte-Real">Gaspar Corte-Real</a> to Greenland in search of a <a href="/wiki/Northwest_Passage" title="Northwest Passage">Northwest Passage</a> to Asia which, according to the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Tordesillas" title="Treaty of Tordesillas">Treaty of Tordesillas</a>, was part of Portugal\'s sphere of influence. In 1501, Corte-Real returned with his brother, <a href="/wiki/Miguel_Corte-Real" title="Miguel Corte-Real">Miguel Corte-Real</a>. Finding the sea frozen, they headed south and arrived in <a href="/wiki/Labrador" title="Labrador">Labrador</a> and <a href="/wiki/Newfoundland_(island)" title="Newfoundland (island)">Newfoundland</a>. Upon the brothers\' return to Portugal, the cartographic information supplied by Corte-Real was incorporated into a new map of the world which was presented to <a href="/wiki/Ercole_I_d%27Este,_Duke_of_Ferrara" title="Ercole I d\'Este, Duke of Ferrara">Ercole I d\'Este</a>, <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Ferrara_and_of_Modena" title="Duke of Ferrara and of Modena">Duke of Ferrara</a>, by Alberto Cantino in 1502. The <a href="/wiki/Cantino_planisphere" title="Cantino planisphere"><i>Cantino</i> planisphere</a>, made in Lisbon, accurately depicts the southern coastline of Greenland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[49]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Old_Greenland_1747.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1307" data-file-width="2048" decoding="async" height="140" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Old_Greenland_1747.jpg/220px-Old_Greenland_1747.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Old_Greenland_1747.jpg/330px-Old_Greenland_1747.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Old_Greenland_1747.jpg/440px-Old_Greenland_1747.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Old_Greenland_1747.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A 1747 map based on Egede\'s descriptions and misconceptions</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1605&#8211;1607, King <a href="/wiki/Christian_IV_of_Denmark" title="Christian IV of Denmark">Christian IV of Denmark</a> sent a <a href="/wiki/Christian_IV%27s_expeditions_to_Greenland" title="Christian IV\'s expeditions to Greenland">series of expeditions</a> to Greenland and Arctic waterways to locate the lost eastern Norse settlement and assert Danish sovereignty over Greenland. The expeditions were mostly unsuccessful, partly due to leaders who lacked experience with the difficult arctic ice and weather conditions, and partly because the expedition leaders were given instructions to search for the Eastern Settlement on the east coast of Greenland just north of <a href="/wiki/Cape_Farewell,_Greenland" title="Cape Farewell, Greenland">Cape Farewell</a>, which is almost inaccessible due to southward <a href="/wiki/Drift_ice" title="Drift ice">drifting ice</a>. The pilot on all three trips was English explorer <a href="/wiki/James_Hall_(explorer)" title="James Hall (explorer)">James Hall</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Legende_b%C3%B8rn,_ca._1878_(8473597948).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1291" data-file-width="1880" decoding="async" height="151" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Legende_b%C3%B8rn%2C_ca._1878_%288473597948%29.jpg/220px-Legende_b%C3%B8rn%2C_ca._1878_%288473597948%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Legende_b%C3%B8rn%2C_ca._1878_%288473597948%29.jpg/330px-Legende_b%C3%B8rn%2C_ca._1878_%288473597948%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Legende_b%C3%B8rn%2C_ca._1878_%288473597948%29.jpg/440px-Legende_b%C3%B8rn%2C_ca._1878_%288473597948%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Legende_b%C3%B8rn,_ca._1878_(8473597948).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Nuuk" title="Nuuk">Godth&#229;b</a> in Greenland, c. 1878</div></div></div>\n<p>After the Norse settlements died off, Greenland came under the de&#160;facto control of various Inuit groups, but the Danish government never forgot or relinquished the claims to Greenland that it had inherited from the Norse. When it re-established contact with Greenland in the early 17th&#160;century, Denmark asserted its sovereignty over the island. In 1721, a joint mercantile and clerical expedition led by Danish-Norwegian missionary <a href="/wiki/Hans_Egede" title="Hans Egede">Hans Egede</a> was sent to Greenland, not knowing whether a Norse civilization remained there. This expedition is part of the Dano-Norwegian colonization of the Americas. After 15&#160;years in Greenland, Hans Egede left his son <a href="/wiki/Paul_Egede" title="Paul Egede">Paul Egede</a> in charge of the mission there and returned to Denmark, where he established a Greenland Seminary. This new colony was centred at <a href="/wiki/Nuuk" title="Nuuk">Godth&#229;b</a> ("Good Hope") on the southwest coast. Gradually, Greenland was opened up to Danish merchants, and closed to those from other countries.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Treaty_of_Kiel_to_World_War_II">Treaty of Kiel to World War II</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Greenland_in_World_War_II" title="Greenland in World War II">Greenland in World War II</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:EricTheRedsLand.gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="470" data-file-width="271" decoding="async" height="295" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/EricTheRedsLand.gif/170px-EricTheRedsLand.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/EricTheRedsLand.gif/255px-EricTheRedsLand.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/c7/EricTheRedsLand.gif 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:EricTheRedsLand.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Eirik Raudes Land</div></div></div>\n<p>When the union between the crowns of Denmark and Norway was dissolved in 1814, the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Kiel" title="Treaty of Kiel">Treaty of Kiel</a> severed Norway\'s former colonies and left them under the control of the Danish monarch. Norway occupied then-uninhabited eastern Greenland as <a href="/wiki/Erik_the_Red%27s_Land" title="Erik the Red\'s Land">Erik the Red\'s Land</a> in July 1931, claiming that it constituted <i><a href="/wiki/Terra_nullius" title="Terra nullius">terra nullius</a></i>. Norway and Denmark agreed to submit the matter in 1933 to the <a href="/wiki/Permanent_Court_of_International_Justice" title="Permanent Court of International Justice">Permanent Court of International Justice</a>, which decided against Norway.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[50]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Greenland\'s connection to Denmark was severed on 9 April 1940, early in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/History_of_Greenland_during_World_War_II" title="History of Greenland during World War II">World War&#160;II</a>, after Denmark was occupied by <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a>. On 8 April 1941, the United States occupied Greenland to defend it against a possible invasion by Germany.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[51]</a></sup> The United States occupation of Greenland continued until 1945. Greenland was able to buy goods from the United States and Canada by selling <a href="/wiki/Cryolite" title="Cryolite">cryolite</a> from the mine at <a href="/wiki/Ivittuut" title="Ivittuut">Ivittuut</a>. The major air bases were <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bluie_West-1" title="Bluie West-1">Bluie West-1</a> at <a href="/wiki/Narsarsuaq_Airport" title="Narsarsuaq Airport">Narsarsuaq</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bluie_West-8" title="Bluie West-8">Bluie West-8</a> at <a href="/wiki/Kangerlussuaq_Airport" title="Kangerlussuaq Airport">S&#248;ndre Str&#248;mfjord</a> (Kangerlussuaq), both of which are still used as Greenland\'s major international airports. <a href="/wiki/Bluie" title="Bluie">Bluie</a> was the military code name for Greenland.\n</p><p>During this war, the system of government changed: <a href="/wiki/List_of_governors_of_Greenland" title="List of governors of Greenland">Governor</a> <a href="/wiki/Eske_Brun" title="Eske Brun">Eske Brun</a> ruled the island under a law of 1925 that allowed governors to take control under extreme circumstances; Governor Aksel Svane was transferred to the United States to lead the commission to supply Greenland. The Danish <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sl%C3%A6depatruljen_Sirius" title="Sl&#230;depatruljen Sirius">Sirius Patrol</a> guarded the northeastern shores of Greenland in 1942 using dogsleds. They detected several German <a href="/wiki/Weather_station" title="Weather station">weather stations</a> and alerted American troops, who destroyed the facilities. After the collapse of the Third Reich, <a href="/wiki/Albert_Speer" title="Albert Speer">Albert Speer</a> briefly considered escaping in a small aeroplane to hide out in Greenland, but changed his mind and decided to surrender to the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Armed_Forces" title="United States Armed Forces">United States Armed Forces</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[52]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Greenland had been a protected and very isolated society until 1940. The <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Denmark" title="Politics of Denmark">Danish government</a> had maintained a strict monopoly of <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Greenland" title="Economy of Greenland">Greenlandic trade</a>, allowing only small scale <a href="/wiki/Troaking" title="Troaking">troaking</a> with Scottish whalers. In wartime Greenland developed a sense of self-reliance through self-government and independent communication with the outside world. Despite this change, in 1946 a commission including the highest Greenlandic council, the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Landsr%C3%A5dene&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Landsr&#229;dene (page does not exist)">Landsr&#229;dene</a>, recommended patience and no radical reform of the system. Two years later, the first step towards a change of government was initiated when a grand commission was established. A final report (G-50) was presented in 1950: Greenland was to be a modern <a href="/wiki/Welfare_state" title="Welfare state">welfare state</a> with Denmark as sponsor and example. In 1953 Greenland was made an equal part of the Danish Kingdom. Home rule was granted in 1979.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Home_rule_and_self-rule">Home rule and self-rule</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Greenlandic_independence" title="Greenlandic independence">Greenlandic independence</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Golfbane_Nuuk.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="4000" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Golfbane_Nuuk.JPG/220px-Golfbane_Nuuk.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Golfbane_Nuuk.JPG/330px-Golfbane_Nuuk.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Golfbane_Nuuk.JPG/440px-Golfbane_Nuuk.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Golfbane_Nuuk.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The orthography and vocabulary of the Greenlandic language is governed by <i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Oqaasileriffik&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Oqaasileriffik (page does not exist)">Oqaasileriffik</a></i>, the Greenlandic language secretariat, located in the <i>Ilimmarfik</i> <a href="/wiki/University_of_Greenland" title="University of Greenland">University of Greenland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nuuk" title="Nuuk">Nuuk</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Following World War II, the United States developed a <a href="/wiki/Geopolitics" title="Geopolitics">geopolitical</a> interest in Greenland, and in 1946 the United States offered to buy the island from Denmark for $100,000,000. Denmark refused to sell it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[54]</a></sup> In the 21st century, the United States, according to <a href="/wiki/WikiLeaks" title="WikiLeaks">WikiLeaks</a>, remains highly interested in investing in the resource base of Greenland and in tapping hydrocarbons off the Greenlandic coast.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[55]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[56]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1950 Denmark agreed to allow the US to reestablish <a href="/wiki/Thule_Air_Base" title="Thule Air Base">Thule Air Base</a> in Greenland; it was greatly expanded between 1951 and 1953 as part of a unified <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a> defense strategy. The local population of three nearby villages was moved more than 100&#160;kilometres (62&#160;mi) away in the winter. The United States tried to construct a subterranean network of secret nuclear missile launch sites in the Greenlandic ice cap, named <a href="/wiki/Project_Iceworm" title="Project Iceworm">Project Iceworm</a>. It managed this project from <a href="/wiki/Camp_Century" title="Camp Century">Camp Century</a> from 1960 to 1966 before abandoning it as unworkable. The Danish government did not become aware of the program\'s mission until 1997, when they discovered it while looking for records related to the <a href="/wiki/1968_Thule_Air_Base_B-52_crash" title="1968 Thule Air Base B-52 crash">crash</a> of a nuclear-equipped <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/B-52" title="B-52">B-52</a>&#160;bomber at Thule in 1968.\n</p><p>With the 1953 Danish constitution, Greenland\'s colonial status ended as the island was incorporated into the Danish realm as an <a href="/wiki/Amt_(country_subdivision)" title="Amt (country subdivision)">amt</a> (county). Danish citizenship was extended to Greenlanders. Danish policies toward Greenland consisted of a strategy of cultural assimilation&#8212;or de-Greenlandification. During this period, the Danish government promoted the exclusive use of the Danish language in official matters, and required Greenlanders to go to Denmark for their post-secondary education. Many Greenlandic children grew up in boarding schools in southern Denmark, and a number lost their cultural ties to Greenland. While the policies "succeeded" in the sense of shifting Greenlanders from being primarily subsistence hunters into being urbanized wage earners, the Greenlandic elite began to reassert a Greenlandic cultural identity. A movement developed in favour of independence, reaching its peak in the 1970s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[57]</a></sup> As a consequence of political complications in relation to Denmark\'s entry into the European Common Market in 1972, Denmark began to seek a different status for Greenland, resulting in the Home Rule Act of 1979.\n</p><p>This gave Greenland limited autonomy with <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Greenland" title="Parliament of Greenland">its own legislature</a> taking control of some internal policies, while the <a href="/wiki/Folketing" title="Folketing">Parliament of Denmark</a> maintained full control of external policies, security, and natural resources. The law came into effect on 1 May 1979. The <a href="/wiki/List_of_Danish_monarchs" title="List of Danish monarchs">Queen of Denmark</a>, <a href="/wiki/Margrethe_II_of_Denmark" title="Margrethe II of Denmark">Margrethe&#160;II</a>, remains Greenland\'s <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">Head of state</a>. In 1985, Greenland left the <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Community" title="European Economic Community">European Economic Community</a> (EEC) upon achieving self-rule, as it did not agree with the EEC\'s commercial fishing regulations and an EEC ban on <a href="/wiki/Pinniped" title="Pinniped">seal</a> skin products.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[58]</a></sup> Greenland voters approved a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greenlandic_self-government_referendum,_2008" title="Greenlandic self-government referendum, 2008">referendum on greater autonomy</a> on 25 November 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[59]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[60]</a></sup> According to one study, the 2008 vote created what "can be seen as a system between home rule and full independence."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[61]</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 21 June 2009, Greenland gained self-rule with provisions for assuming responsibility for self-government of <a href="/wiki/Judiciary" title="Judiciary">judicial affairs</a>, policing, and <a href="/wiki/Natural_resource" title="Natural resource">natural resources</a>. Also, Greenlanders were recognized as a separate people under <a href="/wiki/International_law" title="International law">international law</a>. (<a href="/wiki/One_country,_two_systems" title="One country, two systems">One country, two systems</a>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[62]</a></sup> Denmark maintains control of <a href="/wiki/Foreign_policy" title="Foreign policy">foreign affairs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Military" title="Military">defence</a> matters. Denmark upholds the annual block grant of 3.2&#160;billion Danish kroner, but as Greenland begins to collect revenues of its natural resources, the grant will gradually be diminished. This is generally considered to be a step toward eventual full independence from Denmark.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[63]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Greenlandic_language" title="Greenlandic language">Greenlandic</a> was declared the sole official language of Greenland at the historic ceremony.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-selvstyre_4-2"><a href="#cite_note-selvstyre-4">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-law_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-law-9">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[64]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[65]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[66]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography_and_climate">Geography and climate</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Greenland" title="Geography of Greenland">Geography of Greenland</a></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_Greenland" title="Administrative divisions of Greenland">Administrative divisions of Greenland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Territorial_claims_in_the_Arctic" title="Territorial claims in the Arctic">Territorial claims in the Arctic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_in_the_Arctic" title="Climate change in the Arctic">Climate change in the Arctic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_the_Arctic#Greenland" title="Climate of the Arctic">Climate of the Arctic &#167;&#160;Greenland</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Retreat_of_glaciers_since_1850#Greenland" title="Retreat of glaciers since 1850">Retreat of glaciers since 1850 &#167;&#160;Greenland</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Greenland_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="930" data-file-width="1900" decoding="async" height="127" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Greenland_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/260px-Greenland_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Greenland_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/390px-Greenland_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Greenland_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg/520px-Greenland_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg.png 2x" width="260"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Greenland_map_of_K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Greenland map of K&#246;ppen climate classification</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Greenland_ice_sheet_AMSL_thickness_map-en.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1801" data-file-width="1056" decoding="async" height="290" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Greenland_ice_sheet_AMSL_thickness_map-en.png/170px-Greenland_ice_sheet_AMSL_thickness_map-en.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Greenland_ice_sheet_AMSL_thickness_map-en.png/255px-Greenland_ice_sheet_AMSL_thickness_map-en.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Greenland_ice_sheet_AMSL_thickness_map-en.png/340px-Greenland_ice_sheet_AMSL_thickness_map-en.png 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Greenland_ice_sheet_AMSL_thickness_map-en.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of Greenland</div></div></div>\n<p>Greenland is the world\'s largest non-continental island<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[67]</a></sup> and the third largest country in North America.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[68]</a></sup> It is between latitudes <a href="/wiki/59th_parallel_north" title="59th parallel north">59&#176;</a> and <a href="/wiki/83rd_parallel_north" title="83rd parallel north">83&#176;N</a>, and longitudes <a href="/wiki/11th_meridian_west" title="11th meridian west">11&#176;</a> and <a href="/wiki/74th_meridian_west" title="74th meridian west">74&#176;W</a>. The Atlantic Ocean borders Greenland\'s southeast; the <a href="/wiki/Greenland_Sea" title="Greenland Sea">Greenland Sea</a> is to the east; the Arctic Ocean is to the north; and <a href="/wiki/Baffin_Bay" title="Baffin Bay">Baffin Bay</a> is to the west. The nearest countries are Canada, to the west and southwest across Baffin Bay, and Iceland, east of Greenland in the Atlantic Ocean. Greenland also contains the <a href="/wiki/Northeast_Greenland_National_Park" title="Northeast Greenland National Park">world\'s largest national park</a>, and it is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_and_dependencies_by_area" title="List of countries and dependencies by area">largest</a> <a href="/wiki/Dependent_territory" title="Dependent territory">dependent territory</a> by area in the world, as well as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_the_largest_country_subdivisions_by_area" title="List of the largest country subdivisions by area">fourth largest country subdivision in the world</a>, after <a href="/wiki/Sakha_Republic" title="Sakha Republic">Sakha Republic</a> in <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>\'s state of <a href="/wiki/Western_Australia" title="Western Australia">Western Australia</a>, and Russia\'s <a href="/wiki/Krasnoyarsk_Krai" title="Krasnoyarsk Krai">Krasnoyarsk Krai</a>, and the largest in <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:17-08-islcanus-RalfR-DSC_3282.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3937" data-file-width="5905" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/17-08-islcanus-RalfR-DSC_3282.jpg/220px-17-08-islcanus-RalfR-DSC_3282.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/17-08-islcanus-RalfR-DSC_3282.jpg/330px-17-08-islcanus-RalfR-DSC_3282.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/17-08-islcanus-RalfR-DSC_3282.jpg/440px-17-08-islcanus-RalfR-DSC_3282.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:17-08-islcanus-RalfR-DSC_3282.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Southeast coast of Greenland</div></div></div>\n<p>The average daily temperature of Nuuk, Greenland varies over the seasons from &#8722;8 to 7&#160;&#176;C (18 to 45&#160;&#176;F). The total area of Greenland is 2,166,086&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (836,330&#160;sq&#160;mi) (including other offshore minor islands), of which the <a href="/wiki/Greenland_ice_sheet" title="Greenland ice sheet">Greenland ice sheet</a> covers 1,755,637&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (677,855&#160;sq&#160;mi) (81%) and has a volume of approximately 2,850,000&#160;km<sup>3</sup> (680,000&#160;cu&#160;mi).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[69]</a></sup> The highest point on Greenland is <a href="/wiki/Gunnbj%C3%B8rn_Fjeld" title="Gunnbj&#248;rn Fjeld">Gunnbj&#248;rn Fjeld</a> at 3,700&#160;m (12,139&#160;ft) of the <a href="/wiki/Watkins_Range" title="Watkins Range">Watkins Range</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/East_Greenland_mountain_range" title="East Greenland mountain range">East Greenland mountain range</a>). The majority of Greenland, however, is less than 1,500&#160;m (4,921&#160;ft) in elevation.\n</p><p>The weight of the <a href="/wiki/Ice_sheet" title="Ice sheet">ice sheet</a> has depressed the central land area to form a basin lying more than 300&#160;m (984&#160;ft) below sea level,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[70]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Atlas_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-Atlas-72">[71]</a></sup> while elevations rise suddenly and steeply near the coast.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[72]</a></sup> The ice <a href="/wiki/Ice-sheet_dynamics" title="Ice-sheet dynamics">flows</a> generally to the coast from the centre of the island. A survey led by French scientist <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Paul-Emile_Victor" title="Paul-Emile Victor">Paul-Emile Victor</a> in 1951 concluded that, under the ice sheet, Greenland is composed of three large islands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ellensburg_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-ellensburg-74">[73]</a></sup> This is disputed, but if it is so, they would be separated by narrow straits, reaching the sea at <a href="/wiki/Ilulissat_Icefjord" title="Ilulissat Icefjord">Ilulissat Icefjord</a>, at <a href="/wiki/Greenland%27s_Grand_Canyon" title="Greenland\'s Grand Canyon">Greenland\'s Grand Canyon</a> and south of <a href="/wiki/Nordostrundingen" title="Nordostrundingen">Nordostrundingen</a>.\n</p><p>All <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_and_towns_in_Greenland" title="List of cities and towns in Greenland">towns and settlements of Greenland</a> are situated along the ice-free coast, with the population being concentrated along the west coast. The northeastern part of Greenland is not part of any municipality, but it is the site of the world\'s largest national park, <a href="/wiki/Northeast_Greenland_National_Park" title="Northeast Greenland National Park">Northeast Greenland National Park</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[74]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Greenlandmountains.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1000" data-file-width="750" decoding="async" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Greenlandmountains.jpg/170px-Greenlandmountains.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Greenlandmountains.jpg/255px-Greenlandmountains.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Greenlandmountains.jpg/340px-Greenlandmountains.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Greenlandmountains.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>View of mountains on Greenland from the air</div></div></div>\n<p>At least four scientific expedition stations and camps had been established on the ice sheet in the ice-covered central part of Greenland (indicated as pale blue in the adjacent map): <a href="/wiki/Eismitte" title="Eismitte">Eismitte</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Ice" title="North Ice">North Ice</a>, North GRIP Camp and The Raven Skiway. There is a year-round station <a href="/wiki/Summit_Camp" title="Summit Camp">Summit Camp</a> on the ice sheet, established in 1989. The radio station <a href="/wiki/J%C3%B8rgen_Br%C3%B8nlund_Fjord" title="J&#248;rgen Br&#248;nlund Fjord">J&#248;rgen Br&#248;nlund Fjord</a> was, until 1950, the northernmost permanent outpost in the world.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vatnahverfi.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="400" data-file-width="597" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Vatnahverfi.jpg/220px-Vatnahverfi.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Vatnahverfi.jpg/330px-Vatnahverfi.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Vatnahverfi.jpg/440px-Vatnahverfi.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vatnahverfi.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Southern Greenland is suitable for <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">agriculture</a>. Hay is harvested in <a href="/wiki/Igaliku" title="Igaliku">Igaliku</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kujalleq" title="Kujalleq">Kujalleq</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>The extreme north of Greenland, <a href="/wiki/Peary_Land" title="Peary Land">Peary Land</a>, is not covered by an ice sheet, because the air there is too dry to produce snow, which is essential in the production and maintenance of an ice sheet. If the Greenland ice sheet were to <a href="/wiki/Melting" title="Melting">melt</a> away completely, the world\'s <a href="/wiki/Sea_level" title="Sea level">sea level</a> would rise by more than 7&#160;m (23&#160;ft).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[75]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Between 1989 and 1993, US and European <a href="/wiki/Climate" title="Climate">climate</a> researchers drilled into the summit of Greenland\'s ice sheet, obtaining a pair of 3&#160;km (1.9&#160;mi) long <a href="/wiki/Ice_core" title="Ice core">ice cores</a>. Analysis of the layering and chemical composition of the cores has provided a revolutionary new record of climate change in the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Hemisphere" title="Northern Hemisphere">Northern Hemisphere</a> going back about 100,000&#160;years and illustrated that the world\'s weather and temperature have often shifted rapidly from one seemingly stable state to another, with worldwide <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">consequences</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[76]</a></sup> The glaciers of Greenland are also contributing to a <a href="/wiki/Sea_level_rise" title="Sea level rise">rise in the global sea level</a> faster than was previously believed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-National_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-National-78">[77]</a></sup> Between 1991 and 2004, monitoring of the weather at one location (Swiss Camp) showed that the average winter temperature had risen almost 6&#160;&#176;C (11&#160;&#176;F).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[78]</a></sup> Other research has shown that higher snowfalls from the <a href="/wiki/North_Atlantic_oscillation" title="North Atlantic oscillation">North Atlantic oscillation</a> caused the interior of the ice cap to thicken by an average of 6&#160;cm or 2.36&#160;in/y between 1994 and 2005.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[79]</a></sup> However, a recent study suggests a much warmer planet in relatively recent <a href="/wiki/Geologic_time_scale" title="Geologic time scale">geological times</a>:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pmid17615355_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-pmid17615355-81">[80]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<blockquote>\n<p>Scientists who probed 2&#160;km (1.2&#160;mi) through a Greenland glacier to recover the oldest plant <a href="/wiki/DNA" title="DNA">DNA</a> on record said that the planet was far warmer hundreds of thousands of years ago than is generally believed. DNA of trees, plants, spiders and insects including <a href="/wiki/Butterfly" title="Butterfly">butterflies</a> from beneath the southern Greenland glacier was estimated to date to 450,000 to 900,000&#160;years ago, according to the remnants retrieved from this long-vanished boreal forest. That view contrasts sharply with the prevailing one that a lush forest of this kind could not have existed in Greenland any later than 2.4&#160;million years ago. These DNA samples suggest that the temperature probably reached 10&#160;&#176;C (50&#160;&#176;F) in the summer and &#8722;17&#160;&#176;C (1.4&#160;&#176;F) in the winter. They also indicate that during the <a href="/wiki/Eemian" title="Eemian">last</a> <a href="/wiki/Interglacial" title="Interglacial">interglacial</a> period, 130,000&#8211;116,000&#160;years ago, when local temperatures were on average 5&#160;&#176;C (9&#160;&#176;F) higher than now, the glaciers on Greenland did not completely melt away.\n</p>\n</blockquote>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:442px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Scoresby-sund_view_hg.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1862" data-file-width="6280" decoding="async" height="130" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Scoresby-sund_view_hg.jpg/440px-Scoresby-sund_view_hg.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Scoresby-sund_view_hg.jpg/660px-Scoresby-sund_view_hg.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Scoresby-sund_view_hg.jpg/880px-Scoresby-sund_view_hg.jpg 2x" width="440"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Scoresby-sund_view_hg.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>View of <a href="/wiki/Scoresby_Sound" title="Scoresby Sound">Kangertittivaq</a> in eastern Greenland, one of the largest sund-<a href="/wiki/Fjord" title="Fjord">fjord</a> systems in the world</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Topographic_map_of_Greenland_bedrock.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1042" data-file-width="802" decoding="async" height="221" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Topographic_map_of_Greenland_bedrock.jpg/170px-Topographic_map_of_Greenland_bedrock.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Topographic_map_of_Greenland_bedrock.jpg/255px-Topographic_map_of_Greenland_bedrock.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Topographic_map_of_Greenland_bedrock.jpg/340px-Topographic_map_of_Greenland_bedrock.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Topographic_map_of_Greenland_bedrock.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Greenland bedrock, at current elevation above sea level</div></div></div>\n<p>In 2003, a small island, 35 by 15 metres (115 by 49 feet) in length and width, was discovered by arctic explorer <a href="/wiki/Dennis_Schmitt" title="Dennis Schmitt">Dennis Schmitt</a> and his team at the coordinates of <a href="/wiki/83-42" title="83-42">83-42</a>. Whether this island is permanent is not confirmed as of yet. If it is, it is the northernmost permanent known land on Earth.\n</p><p>In 2007 the existence of a new island was announced. Named "<a href="/wiki/Uunartoq_Qeqertaq" title="Uunartoq Qeqertaq">Uunartoq Qeqertaq</a>" (English: <i>Warming Island</i>), this island has always been present off the coast of Greenland, but was covered by a glacier. This glacier was discovered in 2002 to be shrinking rapidly, and by 2007 had completely melted away, leaving the exposed island.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[81]</a></sup> The island was named Place of the Year by the Oxford Atlas of the World in 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[82]</a></sup> Ben Keene, the atlas\'s editor, commented: "In the last two or three decades, global warming has reduced the size of glaciers throughout the <a href="/wiki/Arctic" title="Arctic">Arctic</a> and earlier this year, news sources confirmed what climate scientists already knew: water, not rock, lay beneath this <a href="/wiki/Ice_bridge" title="Ice bridge">ice bridge</a> on the east coast of Greenland. More islets are likely to appear as the sheet of frozen water covering the world\'s largest island continues to melt".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[83]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Some controversy surrounds the history of the island, specifically over whether the island might have been revealed during a brief warm period in Greenland during the mid-20th&#160;century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[84]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Greenland%27s_Grand_Canyon" title="Greenland\'s Grand Canyon">Greenland\'s Grand Canyon</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Postglacial_glacier_advances_on_the_peninsula_Nuussuaq">Postglacial glacier advances on the peninsula Nuussuaq</span></h3>\n<p>The 1310 m-high Qaqugdluit-mountain-land on the south-side of the peninsula Nuussuaq, situated 50 kilometres (31 miles) west of the Greenland inland ice at <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=Greenland&amp;params=70_7_50_N_51_44_30_W_"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">70&#176;7&#8242;50&#8243;N</span> <span class="longitude">51&#176;44&#8242;30&#8243;W</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">&#65279; / &#65279;</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">70.13056&#176;N 51.74167&#176;W</span><span style="display:none">&#65279; / <span class="geo">70.13056; -51.74167</span></span></span></a></span>, is exemplary of the numerous mountain areas of West-Greenland. Up to the year 1979 (Stage 0) it shows Historical to <a href="/wiki/Holocene" title="Holocene">Holocene</a>, i.e. Postglacial glacier stages dating back at least 7000 and at most about 10 000 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[85]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-W1968_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-W1968-87">[86]</a></sup> In 1979 the glacier tongues came to an end &#8211; according to the extent and height of the glacier nourishing area &#8211; between 660 and 140 metres (2,170 and 460 feet) <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Above_sea_level" title="Above sea level">above sea level</a>. The pertinent climatic glacier snowline (ELA) ran at about 800 metres (2,600 feet) in height. The snowline of the oldest (VII) of the three Holocene glacier stages (V&#8211;VII) ran about 230 metres (750 feet) deeper, i.e. at about 570 metres (1,870 feet) in height.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-K1983_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-K1983-88">[87]</a></sup> The four youngest glacier stages (IV-I) are of a Historical age. They have to be classified as belonging to the global glacier advances in the years 1811 to 1850 and 1880 to 1900 ("Little Ice Age"), 1910 to 1930, 1948 and 1953.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-W1968_87-1"><a href="#cite_note-W1968-87">[86]</a></sup> Their snowlines rose step by step up to the level of 1979. The current snowline (Stage 0) runs nearly unchanged. During the oldest Postglacial Stage VII an ice-stream-network from valley glaciers joining each other, has completely covered the landscape. Its nourishing areas consisted of high-lying plateau-glaciers and local ice caps. Due to the uplift of the snowline about that about 230 metres (750 feet) &#8211; what corresponds to a warming about 1.5&#160;&#176;C (2.7&#160;&#176;F), since 1979 there exists a plateau-glaciation with small glacier tongues hanging down on the margins that nearly did not reach the main valley bottoms any more.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-K1983_88-1"><a href="#cite_note-K1983-88">[87]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Biodiversity">Biodiversity</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Flora_and_fauna_of_Greenland" title="Flora and fauna of Greenland">Flora and fauna of Greenland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Reindeer_hunting_in_Greenland" title="Reindeer hunting in Greenland">Reindeer hunting in Greenland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fishing_industry_in_Greenland" title="Fishing industry in Greenland">Fishing industry in Greenland</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Whaling#Greenland" title="Whaling">Whaling &#167;&#160;Greenland</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Greenland-musk-ox_hg.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1532" data-file-width="2684" decoding="async" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Greenland-musk-ox_hg.jpg/260px-Greenland-musk-ox_hg.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Greenland-musk-ox_hg.jpg/390px-Greenland-musk-ox_hg.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Greenland-musk-ox_hg.jpg/520px-Greenland-musk-ox_hg.jpg 2x" width="260"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Greenland-musk-ox_hg.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Muskox" title="Muskox">Muskox</a> in Greenland</div></div></div>\n<p>There are approximately 700 known species of insects in Greenland, which is low compared with other countries (over one million species have been described worldwide). The sea is rich in fish and invertebrates, especially in the milder <a href="/wiki/West_Greenland_Current" title="West Greenland Current">West Greenland Current</a>, and a large part of the Greenland fauna associated with marine production, including large colonies of seabirds. The few native land mammals in Greenland include the <a href="/wiki/Polar_bear" title="Polar bear">polar bear</a>, <a href="/wiki/Reindeer_hunting_in_Greenland#Three_subspecies_in_Greenland" title="Reindeer hunting in Greenland">reindeer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arctic_fox" title="Arctic fox">arctic fox</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arctic_hare" title="Arctic hare">arctic hare</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Musk_ox" title="Musk ox">musk ox</a>, <a href="/wiki/Northern_collared_lemming" title="Northern collared lemming">collared lemming</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ermine" title="Ermine">ermine</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Arctic_wolf" title="Arctic wolf">arctic wolf</a>. The last four are found naturally only in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/East_Greenland" title="East Greenland">East Greenland</a>, having immigrated from <a href="/wiki/Ellesmere_Island" title="Ellesmere Island">Ellesmere Island</a>. There are dozens of species of <a href="/wiki/Pinniped" title="Pinniped">seals</a> and <a href="/wiki/Whale" title="Whale">whales</a> along the coast. Land fauna consists predominantly of animals that have spread from North America or for a lot of birds and insects coming from Europe. There are no native or free-living reptiles or amphibians on the island.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wildlife_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-wildlife-89">[88]</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Phytogeography" title="Phytogeography">Phytogeographically</a>, Greenland belongs to the Arctic province of the <a href="/wiki/Circumboreal_Region" title="Circumboreal Region">Circumboreal Region</a> within the <a href="/wiki/Boreal_Kingdom" title="Boreal Kingdom">Boreal Kingdom</a>. The island is sparsely populated in vegetation; plant life consists mainly of grassland and small bushes, which is regularly grazed by livestock. The most common tree native to Greenland is the European white birch (<i><a href="/wiki/Betula_pubescens" title="Betula pubescens">Betula pubescens</a></i>) along with gray-leaf willow (<i><a href="/wiki/Salix_glauca" title="Salix glauca">Salix glauca</a></i>), rowans (<i><a href="/wiki/Sorbus_aucuparia" title="Sorbus aucuparia">Sorbus aucuparia</a></i>), common junipers (<i><a href="/wiki/Juniperus_communis" title="Juniperus communis">Juniperus communis</a></i>) and other smaller trees, mainly willows.\n</p><p>Greenland\'s flora comprises about 500 species of higher plants, i.e. <a href="/wiki/Flowering_plant" title="Flowering plant">flowering plants</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fern" title="Fern">ferns</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Horsetail" title="Horsetail">horsetails</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lycopodiophyta" title="Lycopodiophyta">lycopodiophyta</a>. Of the other groups, the <a href="/wiki/Lichen" title="Lichen">lichens</a> are the largest with about 950 species; of major fungal species are known 600&#8211;700; <a href="/wiki/Moss" title="Moss">mosses</a> and <a href="/wiki/Algae" title="Algae">algae</a> anything less. Most of Greenland\'s higher plants are widespread, particularly in arctic and alpine regions, and only a dozen species of particular <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saxifrage" title="Saxifrage">saxifrage</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hawkweed" title="Hawkweed">hawkweed</a> is endemic. A few species were introduced by the Norsemen, such as <a href="/wiki/Vicia_cracca" title="Vicia cracca">cow vetch</a>.\n</p><p>The animals of Greenland include the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greenland_dog" title="Greenland dog">Greenland dog</a>, which was introduced by the <a href="/wiki/Inuit" title="Inuit">Inuit</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_in_Europe" title="Ethnic groups in Europe">European</a>-introduced species such as <a href="/wiki/Greenlandic_sheep" title="Greenlandic sheep">Greenlandic sheep</a>, <a href="/wiki/Goat" title="Goat">goats</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cattle" title="Cattle">cattle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Reindeer" title="Reindeer">reindeer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Horse" title="Horse">horse</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chicken" title="Chicken">chicken</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sheepdog" title="Sheepdog">sheepdog</a>, all descendants of animals imported by Europeans. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marine_mammals" title="Marine mammals">Marine mammals</a> include the <a href="/wiki/Hooded_seal" title="Hooded seal">hooded seal</a> (<i>Cystophora cristata</i>) as well as the <a href="/wiki/Grey_seal" title="Grey seal">grey seal</a> (<i>Halichoerus grypus</i>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-brit1911_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-brit1911-90">[89]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Whale" title="Whale">Whales</a> frequently pass very close to Greenlandic shores in the late summer and early autumn. Species represented include the <a href="/wiki/Beluga_whale" title="Beluga whale">beluga whale</a>, <a href="/wiki/Blue_whale" title="Blue whale">blue whale</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bowhead_whale" title="Bowhead whale">Greenland whale</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fin_whale" title="Fin whale">fin whale</a>, <a href="/wiki/Humpback_whale" title="Humpback whale">humpback whale</a>, <a href="/wiki/Minke_whale" title="Minke whale">minke whale</a>, <a href="/wiki/Narwhal" title="Narwhal">narwhal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pilot_whale" title="Pilot whale">pilot whale</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sperm_whale" title="Sperm whale">sperm whale</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guide_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-guide-91">[90]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Approximately 225 species of fish are known from the waters surrounding Greenland, and the <a href="/wiki/Fishing_industry" title="Fishing industry">fishing industry</a> is a major part of Greenland\'s economy, accounting for the majority of the country\'s total exports.\n</p><p>Birds, especially seabirds, are an important part of Greenland\'s animal life. On steep mountainsides breed large colonies of <a href="/wiki/Auk" title="Auk">auks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Puffin" title="Puffin">puffins</a>, <a href="/wiki/Skua" title="Skua">skuas</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kittiwake" title="Kittiwake">kittiwakes</a>. By common ducks include <a href="/wiki/Eider" title="Eider">eiders</a>, <a href="/wiki/Long-tailed_duck" title="Long-tailed duck">long-tailed ducks</a> and the <a href="/wiki/King_eider" title="King eider">king eider</a> and in West Greenland <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White-fronted_goose" title="White-fronted goose">white-fronted goose</a> and in East Greenland <a href="/wiki/Pink-footed_goose" title="Pink-footed goose">pink-footed goose</a> and <a href="/wiki/Barnacle_goose" title="Barnacle goose">barnacle goose</a>. Breeding migratory birds are also including <a href="/wiki/Snow_bunting" title="Snow bunting">snow bunting</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lapland_bunting" title="Lapland bunting">lapland bunting</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ringed_plover" title="Ringed plover">ringed plover</a>, <a href="/wiki/Red-throated_loon" title="Red-throated loon">red-throated loon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Red-necked_phalarope" title="Red-necked phalarope">red-necked phalarope</a>. Of land birds that are usually sedentary, can be highlighted <a href="/wiki/Arctic_redpoll" title="Arctic redpoll">arctic redpoll</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rock_ptarmigan" title="Rock ptarmigan">ptarmigan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Short-eared_owl" title="Short-eared owl">short-eared owl</a>, <a href="/wiki/Snowy_owl" title="Snowy owl">snowy owl</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gyrfalcon" title="Gyrfalcon">gyrfalcon</a> and in West Greenland the <a href="/wiki/White-tailed_eagle" title="White-tailed eagle">white-tailed eagle</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wildlife_89-1"><a href="#cite_note-wildlife-89">[88]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Greenland" title="Politics of Greenland">Politics of Greenland</a></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Denmark" title="Politics of Denmark">Politics of Denmark</a>, <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_the_Faroe_Islands" title="Politics of the Faroe Islands">Politics of the Faroe Islands</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Greenland%E2%80%93European_Union_relations" title="Greenland&#8211;European Union relations">Greenland&#8211;European Union relations</a></div>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303569">@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti>.thumbinner{width:100%!important;max-width:none!important}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:none!important;width:100%!important;text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:434px;max-width:434px"><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:150px;max-width:150px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Drottning_Margrethe_av_Danmark_crop.jpg"><img alt="" 1972</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:131px;max-width:131px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kim_Kielsen._Nordiska_raoedets_session_i_Helsingfors_2012.jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="5184" data-file-width="3456" decoding="async" height="194" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Kim_Kielsen._Nordiska_raoedets_session_i_Helsingfors_2012.jpg/258px-Kim_Kielsen._Nordiska_raoedets_session_i_Helsingfors_2012.jpg 2x" width="129"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Kim_Kielsen" title="Kim Kielsen">Kim Kielsen</a>,<br/> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Premier_of_Greenland" title="Premier of Greenland">Premier</a> since 2014</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:147px;max-width:147px"><div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Danmarks_statsminister_Lars_Loekke_Rasmussen_pa_Nordiska_radets_session_i_Reykjavik_2010_(1).jpg"><img alt="" data-file-height="3801" data-file-width="2823" decoding="async"
