1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Danmarks_statsminister_Lars_Loekke_Rasmussen_pa_Nordiska_radets_session_i_Reykjavik_2010_%281%29.jpg/290px-Danmarks_statsminister_Lars_Loekke_Rasmussen_pa_Nordiska_radets_session_i_Reykjavik_2010_%281%29.jpg 2x" width="145"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left"><a href="/wiki/Lars_L%C3%B8kke_Rasmussen" title="Lars L&#248;kke Rasmussen">Lars L&#248;kke Rasmussen</a>,<br/> <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Denmark" title="Prime Minister of Denmark">Prime Minister</a> since 2015</div></div><div style="clear:left"></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Central_administration_of_Greenland.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2560" data-file-width="1920" decoding="async" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Central_administration_of_Greenland.jpg/220px-Central_administration_of_Greenland.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Central_administration_of_Greenland.jpg/330px-Central_administration_of_Greenland.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Central_administration_of_Greenland.jpg/440px-Central_administration_of_Greenland.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Central_administration_of_Greenland.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Greenland Government Building</div></div></div>\n<p>The Kingdom of Denmark is a <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional monarchy</a>, in which <a href="/wiki/Margrethe_II_of_Denmark" title="Margrethe II of Denmark">Queen Margrethe II</a> is the head of state. The monarch officially retains <a href="/wiki/Executive_(government)" title="Executive (government)">executive power</a> and presides over the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Danish_Council_of_State" title="Danish Council of State">Council of State</a> (<a href="/wiki/Privy_council" title="Privy council">privy council</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[91]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[92]</a></sup> However, following the introduction of a <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_system" title="Parliamentary system">parliamentary system</a> of government, the duties of the monarch have since become strictly representative and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ceremonial" title="Ceremonial">ceremonial</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[93]</a></sup> such as the formal appointment and dismissal of the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Denmark" title="Prime Minister of Denmark">Prime Minister</a> and other ministers in the executive government. The monarch is not answerable for his or her actions, and the monarch\'s person is sacrosanct.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[94]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_system">Political system</span></h3>\n<p>The party system is dominated by the social-democratic <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Forward_(Greenland)" title="Forward (Greenland)">Forward</a> Party, and the democratic socialist <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Inuit_Community" title="Inuit Community">Inuit Community</a> Party, both of which broadly argue for greater independence from Denmark. While the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greenlandic_parliamentary_election,_2009" title="Greenlandic parliamentary election, 2009">2009 election</a> saw the unionist&#8212;and largely Danish&#8212;<a href="/wiki/Democrats_(Greenland)" title="Democrats (Greenland)">Democrat</a> Party (2&#160;MPs) decline greatly, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greenlandic_parliamentary_election,_2013" title="Greenlandic parliamentary election, 2013">2013 election</a> consolidated the power of the two main parties at the expense of the smaller groups, and saw the <a href="/wiki/Eco-socialism" title="Eco-socialism">eco-socialist</a> <a href="/wiki/Inuit_Party" title="Inuit Party">Inuit Party</a>  elected to the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Greenland" title="Parliament of Greenland">Parliament</a> for the first time. The dominance of the Forward and Inuit Community parties began to wane after the snap <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greenlandic_general_election,_2014" title="Greenlandic general election, 2014">2014</a> elections, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greenlandic_general_election,_2018" title="Greenlandic general election, 2018">2018</a> elections.\n</p><p>The non-binding <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greenlandic_self-government_referendum,_2008" title="Greenlandic self-government referendum, 2008">2008 referendum on self-governance</a> favoured increased self-governance 21,355 votes to 6,663.\n</p><p>In 1985, <a href="/wiki/Greenland%E2%80%93European_Union_relations" title="Greenland&#8211;European Union relations">Greenland left the European Economic Community</a> (EEC), unlike Denmark, which remains a member. The EEC later became the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> (EU, renamed and expanded in scope in 1992). Greenland retains some ties with the EU via Denmark. However, EU law largely does not apply to Greenland except in the area of trade.  Greenland is a member state of the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Europe" title="Council of Europe">Council of Europe</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47_Member_States_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-47_Member_States-96">[95]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Greenland" title="Politics of Greenland">Politics of Greenland</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Greenland-municipalities-2018.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="300" decoding="async" height="283" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Greenland-municipalities-2018.svg/170px-Greenland-municipalities-2018.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Greenland-municipalities-2018.svg/255px-Greenland-municipalities-2018.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Greenland-municipalities-2018.svg/340px-Greenland-municipalities-2018.svg.png 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Greenland-municipalities-2018.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Municipalities of Greenland</div></div></div>\n<p>Greenland\'s <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a> is <a href="/wiki/Margrethe_II_of_Denmark" title="Margrethe II of Denmark">Margrethe&#160;II</a>, <a href="/wiki/Queen_regnant" title="Queen regnant">Queen regnant</a> of Denmark. The Queen\'s <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Denmark" title="Politics of Denmark">government in Denmark</a> appoints a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Danish_High_Commissioners_in_Greenland" title="List of Danish High Commissioners in Greenland">High Commissioner</a> (<i>Rigsombudsmand</i>) to represent it on the island. The commissioner is <a href="/wiki/Mikaela_Engell" title="Mikaela Engell">Mikaela Engell</a>.\n</p><p>Greenlanders elect two representatives to the <a href="/wiki/Folketing" title="Folketing">Folketing</a>, Denmark\'s parliament, out of a total of 179. The representatives are <a href="/wiki/Aleqa_Hammond" title="Aleqa Hammond">Aleqa Hammond</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Siumut" title="Siumut">Siumut</a> Party and <a href="/wiki/Aaja_Chemnitz_Larsen" title="Aaja Chemnitz Larsen">Aaja Chemnitz Larsen</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Inuit_Community" title="Inuit Community">Inuit Community</a> Party.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[96]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Greenland also has its own <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Greenland" title="Parliament of Greenland">Parliament</a>, which has 31&#160;members. The government is the <a href="/wiki/Naalakkersuisut" title="Naalakkersuisut">Naalakkersuisut</a> whose members are appointed by the Premier. The <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a> is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Premiers_of_Greenland" title="List of Premiers of Greenland">Premier</a>, usually the leader of the majority party in Parliament. The Premier is <a href="/wiki/Kim_Kielsen" title="Kim Kielsen">Kim Kielsen</a> of the Siumut Party.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_Greenland" title="Administrative divisions of Greenland">Administrative divisions of Greenland</a></div>\n<p>Formerly consisting of three counties comprising a total of 18 municipalities, Greenland abolished these in 2009 and has since been divided into large territories known as "municipalities" (<a href="/wiki/Greenlandic_language" title="Greenlandic language">Greenlandic</a>: <i lang="kl">kommuneqarfiit</i>, <a href="/wiki/Danish_language" title="Danish language">Danish</a>: <i lang="da">kommuner</i>): <i><a href="/wiki/Sermersooq" title="Sermersooq">Sermersooq</a></i> ("Much Ice") around the capital <a href="/wiki/Nuuk" title="Nuuk">Nuuk</a> and also including all <a href="/wiki/Tunu" title="Tunu">East Coast</a> communities; <i><a href="/wiki/Kujalleq" title="Kujalleq">Kujalleq</a></i> ("South") around <a href="/wiki/Cape_Farewell,_Greenland" title="Cape Farewell, Greenland">Cape Farewell</a>; <i><a href="/wiki/Qeqqata" title="Qeqqata">Qeqqata</a></i> ("Centre") north of the capital along the <a href="/wiki/Davis_Strait" title="Davis Strait">Davis Strait</a>; <i><a href="/wiki/Qeqertalik" title="Qeqertalik">Qeqertalik</a></i> ("The one with islands") surrounding <a href="/wiki/Disko_Bay" title="Disko Bay">Disko Bay</a>; and <i><a href="/wiki/Avannaata" title="Avannaata">Avannaata</a></i> ("Northern") in the northwest; the latter two having come into being as a result of the <a href="/wiki/Qaasuitsup" title="Qaasuitsup">Qaasuitsup</a> municipality, one of the original four, being partitioned in 2018. The northeast of the island composes the unincorporated <i><a href="/wiki/Northeast_Greenland_National_Park" title="Northeast Greenland National Park">Northeast Greenland National Park</a></i>. <i><a href="/wiki/Thule_Air_Base" title="Thule Air Base">Thule Air Base</a></i> is also unincorporated, an enclave within Avannaata municipality administered by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Air_Force" title="United States Air Force">United States Air Force</a>. During its construction, there were as many as 12,000 American residents but in recent years the number has been below 1,000.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Greenland" title="Economy of Greenland">Economy of Greenland</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Greenland_Export_Treemap.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2086" data-file-width="2668" decoding="async" height="172" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Greenland_Export_Treemap.jpg/220px-Greenland_Export_Treemap.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Greenland_Export_Treemap.jpg/330px-Greenland_Export_Treemap.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a0/Greenland_Export_Treemap.jpg/440px-Greenland_Export_Treemap.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Greenland_Export_Treemap.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Graphical depiction of Greenland\'s product exports in 28 colour-coded categories</div></div></div>\n<p>The Greenlandic economy is highly dependent on fishing. Fishing accounts for more than 90% of Greenland\'s exports.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-98">[97]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Shrimp" title="Shrimp">shrimp</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fish" title="Fish">fish</a> industry is by far the largest income earner.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia-factbook_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-cia-factbook-3">[2]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Greenland is abundant in minerals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_98-1"><a href="#cite_note-:0-98">[97]</a></sup> Mining of <a href="/wiki/Ruby" title="Ruby">ruby</a> deposits began in 2007. Other mineral prospects are improving as prices are increasing. These include iron, <a href="/wiki/Uranium" title="Uranium">uranium</a>, aluminium, nickel, <a href="/wiki/Platinum" title="Platinum">platinum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tungsten" title="Tungsten">tungsten</a>, <a href="/wiki/Titanium" title="Titanium">titanium</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Copper" title="Copper">copper</a>. Despite resumption<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (January 2014)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> of several <a href="/wiki/Hydrocarbon" title="Hydrocarbon">hydrocarbon</a> and mineral exploration activities, it will take several years before hydrocarbon production can materialize. The state oil company <a href="/wiki/Nunaoil" title="Nunaoil">Nunaoil</a> was created to help develop the hydrocarbon industry in Greenland. The state company Nunamineral has been launched on the <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen_Stock_Exchange" title="Copenhagen Stock Exchange">Copenhagen Stock Exchange</a> to raise more capital to increase the production of gold, started in 2007.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tasiilaq.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3072" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Tasiilaq.jpg/220px-Tasiilaq.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Tasiilaq.jpg/330px-Tasiilaq.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Tasiilaq.jpg/440px-Tasiilaq.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tasiilaq.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Tasiilaq is a town in the <a href="/wiki/Sermersooq" title="Sermersooq">Sermersooq</a> municipality in southeastern Greenland</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Akamalik-royal-greenland-sisimiut-port.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2176" data-file-width="3872" decoding="async" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Akamalik-royal-greenland-sisimiut-port.jpg/220px-Akamalik-royal-greenland-sisimiut-port.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Akamalik-royal-greenland-sisimiut-port.jpg/330px-Akamalik-royal-greenland-sisimiut-port.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Akamalik-royal-greenland-sisimiut-port.jpg/440px-Akamalik-royal-greenland-sisimiut-port.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Akamalik-royal-greenland-sisimiut-port.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Royal_Greenland" title="Royal Greenland">Royal Greenland</a> fishing vessel "Akamalik", anchored at <a href="/wiki/Sisimiut" title="Sisimiut">Sisimiut</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Electricity has traditionally been generated by oil or diesel power plants, even if there is a large surplus of potential <a href="/wiki/Hydropower" title="Hydropower">hydropower</a>. There is a programme to build hydro power plants. The first, and still the largest, is <a href="/wiki/Buksefjord_hydroelectric_power_plant" title="Buksefjord hydroelectric power plant">Buksefjord hydroelectric power plant</a>.\n</p><p>There are also plans to build a large aluminium smelter, using hydropower to create an exportable product. It is expected that much of the labour needed will be imported.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[98]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> has urged Greenland to restrict People\'s Republic of China development of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rare-earth" title="Rare-earth">rare-earth</a> projects, as China accounts for 95% of the world\'s current supply. In early 2013, the Greenland government said that it had no plans to impose such restrictions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[99]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The public sector, including publicly owned enterprises and the municipalities, plays a dominant role in Greenland\'s economy. About half the government revenues come from grants from the Danish government, an important supplement to the gross domestic product (GDP). Gross domestic product per capita is equivalent to that of the average economies of Europe.\n</p><p>Greenland suffered an economic contraction in the early 1990s. But, since 1993, the economy has improved. The Greenland Home Rule Government (GHRG) has pursued a tight fiscal policy since the late 1980s, which has helped create surpluses in the public budget and low inflation. Since 1990, Greenland has registered a foreign-trade deficit following the closure of the last remaining lead and <a href="/wiki/Zinc" title="Zinc">zinc</a> mine that year. More recently,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (January 2014)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> new sources of <a href="/wiki/Ruby" title="Ruby">ruby</a> in Greenland have been discovered, promising to bring new industry and a new export from the country. (See <a href="/wiki/Gemstone_industry_in_Greenland" title="Gemstone industry in Greenland">Gemstone industry in Greenland</a>).\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Greenland" title="Transport in Greenland">Transport in Greenland</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_airports_in_Greenland" title="List of airports in Greenland">List of airports in Greenland</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:AirGreenland_Airbus_(11832722805).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1050" data-file-width="1500" decoding="async" height="154" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/AirGreenland_Airbus_%2811832722805%29.jpg/220px-AirGreenland_Airbus_%2811832722805%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/AirGreenland_Airbus_%2811832722805%29.jpg/330px-AirGreenland_Airbus_%2811832722805%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/AirGreenland_Airbus_%2811832722805%29.jpg/440px-AirGreenland_Airbus_%2811832722805%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:AirGreenland_Airbus_(11832722805).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Air_Greenland" title="Air Greenland">Air Greenland</a> Airbus <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/A330-200" title="A330-200">A330-200</a> in-flight</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Town_of_Ilulissat,_Greenland,_as_Seen_From_Secretary_Kerry%27s_Plane_(27795542865).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3077" data-file-width="4616" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/The_Town_of_Ilulissat%2C_Greenland%2C_as_Seen_From_Secretary_Kerry%27s_Plane_%2827795542865%29.jpg/220px-The_Town_of_Ilulissat%2C_Greenland%2C_as_Seen_From_Secretary_Kerry%27s_Plane_%2827795542865%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/The_Town_of_Ilulissat%2C_Greenland%2C_as_Seen_From_Secretary_Kerry%27s_Plane_%2827795542865%29.jpg/330px-The_Town_of_Ilulissat%2C_Greenland%2C_as_Seen_From_Secretary_Kerry%27s_Plane_%2827795542865%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/The_Town_of_Ilulissat%2C_Greenland%2C_as_Seen_From_Secretary_Kerry%27s_Plane_%2827795542865%29.jpg/440px-The_Town_of_Ilulissat%2C_Greenland%2C_as_Seen_From_Secretary_Kerry%27s_Plane_%2827795542865%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Town_of_Ilulissat,_Greenland,_as_Seen_From_Secretary_Kerry%27s_Plane_(27795542865).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The port of <a href="/wiki/Ilulissat" title="Ilulissat">Ilulissat</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Air transportation exists both within Greenland and between the island and other nations. There is also scheduled boat traffic, but the long distances lead to long travel times and low frequency. There are virtually no roads between cities because the coast has many fjords that would require ferry service to connect a road network. The only exception is a gravel road of 3 miles length between <a href="/wiki/Kangilinnguit" title="Kangilinnguit">Kangilinnguit</a> and the now abandoned former <a href="/wiki/Cryolite" title="Cryolite">cryolite</a> mining town of <a href="/wiki/Ivittuut" title="Ivittuut">Ivittuut</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-iExplore_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-iExplore-101">[100]</a></sup> In addition, the lack of agriculture, forestry and similar countryside activities has meant that very few countryside roads have been built.\n</p><p>All civil aviation matters are handled by the <a href="/wiki/Danish_Transport_Authority" title="Danish Transport Authority">Danish Transport Authority</a>. Most airports including <a href="/wiki/Nuuk_Airport" title="Nuuk Airport">Nuuk Airport</a> have short runways and can only be served by special fairly small aircraft on fairly short flights. <a href="/wiki/Kangerlussuaq_Airport" title="Kangerlussuaq Airport">Kangerlussuaq Airport</a> around 100 kilometres (62 miles) inland from the west coast is the major airport of Greenland and the hub for domestic flights. Intercontinental flights connect mainly to <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen" title="Copenhagen">Copenhagen</a>. Travel between international destinations (except Iceland) and any city in Greenland requires a plane change.\n</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Air_Iceland" title="Air Iceland">Air Iceland</a> operates flights from <a href="/wiki/Reykjav%C3%ADk" title="Reykjav&#237;k">Reykjav&#237;k</a> to a number of airports in Greenland, and the company promotes the service as a day-trip option from Iceland for tourists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[101]</a></sup>\n</p><p>There are no direct flights to the United States or Canada, although there have been flights Kangerlussuaq &#8211; <a href="/wiki/Baltimore" title="Baltimore">Baltimore</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[102]</a></sup> and Nuuk &#8211; <a href="/wiki/Iqaluit" title="Iqaluit">Iqaluit</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[103]</a></sup> which were cancelled because of too few passengers and financial losses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[104]</a></sup> An alternative between Greenland and the United States/Canada is Air Iceland/<a href="/wiki/Icelandair" title="Icelandair">Icelandair</a> with a plane change in Iceland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[105]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Sea <a href="/wiki/Passenger" title="Passenger">passenger</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cargo" title="Cargo">freight</a> transport is served by the coastal ferries operated by <a href="/wiki/Arctic_Umiaq_Line" title="Arctic Umiaq Line">Arctic Umiaq Line</a>. It makes a single round trip per week, taking 80 hours each direction.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Population">Population</span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Greenland" title="Demographics of Greenland">Demographics of Greenland</a></div> <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Greenlanders" title="List of Greenlanders">List of Greenlanders</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kulusuk,_Inuit_couple_(6822265499).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2848" data-file-width="4272" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Kulusuk%2C_Inuit_couple_%286822265499%29.jpg/220px-Kulusuk%2C_Inuit_couple_%286822265499%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Kulusuk%2C_Inuit_couple_%286822265499%29.jpg/330px-Kulusuk%2C_Inuit_couple_%286822265499%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Kulusuk%2C_Inuit_couple_%286822265499%29.jpg/440px-Kulusuk%2C_Inuit_couple_%286822265499%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kulusuk,_Inuit_couple_(6822265499).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Tunumiit" title="Tunumiit">Tunumiit</a> <a href="/wiki/Inuit" title="Inuit">Inuit</a> couple from <a href="/wiki/Kulusuk" title="Kulusuk">Kulusuk</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Greenland has a population of 56,370 (January 2013 estimate),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Greenland_in_Figures_2013_7-2"><a href="#cite_note-Greenland_in_Figures_2013-7">[6]</a></sup> of whom 88% are <a href="/wiki/Greenlandic_Inuit" title="Greenlandic Inuit">Greenlandic Inuit</a> (including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Danish_people" title="Danish people">Danish</a>-<a href="/wiki/Inuit" title="Inuit">Inuit</a> mixed). The remaining 12% are of <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_groups_in_Europe" title="Ethnic groups in Europe">European</a> descent, mainly <a href="/wiki/Danish_people_in_Greenland" title="Danish people in Greenland">Greenland Danes</a>. Several thousand <a href="/wiki/Greenlandic_people_in_Denmark" title="Greenlandic people in Denmark">Greenlandic Inuit reside in the Danish Peninsula</a>. The majority of the population is <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Denmark" title="Church of Denmark">Lutheran</a>. Nearly all Greenlanders live along the fjords in the south-west of the main island, which has a relatively mild climate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[106]</a></sup> More than 17,000 people reside in <a href="/wiki/Nuuk" title="Nuuk">Nuuk</a>, the capital city.\n</p><p><br/>\n</p>\n<table class="navbox">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th style="text-align:right;">355\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align:center;background:#f0f0f0;">10</td>\n<td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Paamiut" title="Paamiut">Paamiut</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Sermersooq" title="Sermersooq">Sermersooq</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">1,334</td>\n<td style="text-align:center;background:#f0f0f0;">20</td>\n<td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Kangaamiut" title="Kangaamiut">Kangaamiut</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:left;"><a href="/wiki/Qeqqata" title="Qeqqata">Qeqqata</a></td>\n<td style="text-align:right;">304\n</td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n<p><br/>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Parkverbot_Gr%C3%B6nland.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="640" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Parkverbot_Gr%C3%B6nland.jpg/220px-Parkverbot_Gr%C3%B6nland.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Parkverbot_Gr%C3%B6nland.jpg/330px-Parkverbot_Gr%C3%B6nland.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Parkverbot_Gr%C3%B6nland.jpg/440px-Parkverbot_Gr%C3%B6nland.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Parkverbot_Gr%C3%B6nland.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A bilingual sign in Nuuk, displaying the Danish and Kalaallisut for "Parking forbidden for all vehicles"</div></div></div>\n<p>Both <a href="/wiki/Greenlandic_language" title="Greenlandic language">Greenlandic</a> (an <a href="/wiki/Eskimo%E2%80%93Aleut_languages" title="Eskimo&#8211;Aleut languages">Eskimo&#8211;Aleut</a> language) and <a href="/wiki/Danish_language" title="Danish language">Danish</a> have been used in public affairs since the establishment of home rule in 1979; the majority of the population can speak both languages. Greenlandic became the sole official language in June 2009,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[108]</a></sup> In practice, Danish is still widely used in the administration and in higher education, as well as remaining the first or only language for some Danish immigrants in Nuuk and other larger towns. Debate about the roles of Greenlandic and Danish in the country\'s future is ongoing. The orthography of Greenlandic was established in 1851<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[109]</a></sup> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kalaallisut_orthography" title="Kalaallisut orthography">revised</a> in 1973. The country has a 100% literacy rate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia-factbook_3-2"><a href="#cite_note-cia-factbook-3">[2]</a></sup>\n</p><p>A majority of the population speaks Greenlandic, most of them bilingually. It is spoken by about 50,000 people, making it the most populous of the Eskimo&#8211;Aleut language family, spoken by more people than all the other languages of the family combined.\n</p><p>Kalaallisut is the Greenlandic dialect of West Greenland, which has long been the most populous area of the island. This has led to its de&#160;facto status as the official "Greenlandic" language, although the northern dialect <a href="/wiki/Inuktun" title="Inuktun">Inuktun</a> remains spoken by 1,000 or so people around <a href="/wiki/Qaanaaq" title="Qaanaaq">Qaanaaq</a>, and the eastern dialect <a href="/wiki/Tunumiit_dialect" title="Tunumiit dialect">Tunumiisut</a> by around 3,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[110]</a></sup> Each of these dialects is almost unintelligible to the speakers of the other and are considered by some linguists to be separate languages.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> A <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> report has labelled the other dialects as endangered, and measures are now being considered to protect the East Greenlandic dialects.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[111]</a></sup>\n</p><p>About 12% of the population speak Danish as a first or sole language, particularly Danish immigrants in Greenland, many of whom fill positions such as administrators, professionals, academics, or skilled tradesmen. While Greenlandic is dominant in all smaller settlements, a part of the population of Inuit or mixed ancestry, especially in towns, speaks Danish. Most of the Inuit population speaks Danish as a second language. In larger towns, especially Nuuk and in the higher social strata, this is still a large group. While one strategy aims at promoting Greenlandic in public life and education, developing its vocabulary and suitability for all complex contexts, there are opponents of this.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>\n</p><p>English is another important language for Greenland, taught in schools from the first school year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[112]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Greenland" title="Religion in Greenland">Religion in Greenland</a></div>\n<div class="PieChartTemplate thumb tright" style=""><div class="thumbinner" style="width:200px">\n<div style="background-color:white;margin:auto;position:relative;width:200px;height:200px;overflow:hidden;border-radius:100px;border:1px solid black">\n<div style="border:solid style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:Turquoise"></div>\n<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:Turquoise"></div><div style="border:solid style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:DarkOrchid"></div>\n<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:DarkOrchid"></div><div style="border:solid transparent;position:absolute;width:100px;line-height:0;left:100px; top:100px; border-width:100px 0 0 344.20225766694px; border-left-color:DodgerBlue"></div>\n<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 200px 100px 0;border-color:DodgerBlue"></div>\n<div style="position:absolute;line-height:0;border-style:solid;left:0;top:0;border-width:0 100px 200px 0;border-color:DodgerBlue"></div>\n</div>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<p>Religion in Greenland (2010)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ARDA_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-ARDA-114">[113]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[114]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:DodgerBlue; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestantism</a> (95.5%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:DarkOrchid; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism" title="Roman Catholicism">Roman Catholicism</a> (0.2%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Turquoise; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Other <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christian</a> (0.4%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Red; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Inuit_spiritual_beliefs" title="Inuit spiritual beliefs">Inuit spiritual beliefs</a> (0.8%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Honeydew; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Agnostic" title="Agnostic">Agnostic</a> (2.3%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Grey; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atheist" title="Atheist">Atheist</a> (0.2%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Yellow; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Other Religion (0.6%)</div>\n</div>\n</div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nanortalik_church.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1348" data-file-width="2560" decoding="async" height="116" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Nanortalik_church.jpg/220px-Nanortalik_church.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Nanortalik_church.jpg/330px-Nanortalik_church.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Nanortalik_church.jpg/440px-Nanortalik_church.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nanortalik_church.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Most Greenlandic villages, including <a href="/wiki/Nanortalik" title="Nanortalik">Nanortalik</a>, have their own church.</div></div></div>\n<p>The nomadic <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Inuit_people" title="Inuit people">Inuit people</a> were traditionally <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shamanism_among_Eskimo_peoples" title="Shamanism among Eskimo peoples">shamanistic</a>, with a well-developed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Inuit_mythology" title="Inuit mythology">mythology</a> primarily concerned with appeasing a vengeful and <a href="/wiki/Sedna_(mythology)" title="Sedna (mythology)">fingerless sea goddess</a> who controlled the success of the <a href="/wiki/Seal_hunting" title="Seal hunting">seal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Whaling" title="Whaling">whale hunts</a>.\n</p><p>The first <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Norse_colonization_of_Greenland" title="Norse colonization of Greenland">Norse colonists</a> worshipped the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Norse_religion" title="Norse religion">Norse gods</a>, but <a href="/wiki/Erik_the_Red" title="Erik the Red">Erik the Red</a>\'s son <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Leif_Ericson" title="Leif Ericson">Leif</a> was converted to Christianity by <a href="/wiki/List_of_Norwegian_monarchs" title="List of Norwegian monarchs">King</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Olaf_Trygvesson" title="Olaf Trygvesson">Olaf Trygvesson</a> on a trip to Norway in 999 and sent missionaries back to Greenland. These swiftly established sixteen parishes, some monasteries, and a bishopric at <a href="/wiki/Gar%C3%B0ar,_Greenland" title="Gar&#240;ar, Greenland">Gar&#240;ar</a>.\n</p><p>Rediscovering these colonists and spreading ideas of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Danish_Reformation" title="Danish Reformation">Protestant Reformation</a> among them was one of the primary reasons for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Danish_colonization_of_Greenland" title="Danish colonization of Greenland">Danish recolonization</a> in the 18th century. Under the patronage of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Royal_Mission_College" title="Royal Mission College">Royal Mission College</a> in Copenhagen, Norwegian and Danish <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Denmark" title="Church of Denmark">Lutherans</a> and German <a href="/wiki/Moravian_missions_in_Greenland" title="Moravian missions in Greenland">Moravian missionaries</a> searched for the missing Norse settlements, but no Norse were found, and instead they began preaching to the Inuit. The principal figures in the <a href="/wiki/Christianization" title="Christianization">Christianization</a> of Greenland were <a href="/wiki/Hans_Egede" title="Hans Egede">Hans</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Poul_Egede" title="Poul Egede">Poul Egede</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Matthias_Stach" title="Matthias Stach">Matthias Stach</a>. The <a href="/wiki/New_Testament" title="New Testament">New Testament</a> was translated piecemeal from the time of the very first settlement on Kangeq Island, but the first translation of the whole Bible was not completed until 1900. An improved translation using the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kalaallisut_orthography" title="Kalaallisut orthography">modern orthography</a> was completed in 2000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[115]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Today, the major religion is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protestant" title="Protestant">Protestant</a> <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a>, represented mainly by the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Denmark" title="Church of Denmark">Church of Denmark</a>, which is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lutheran" title="Lutheran">Lutheran</a> in orientation. While there are no official census data on religion in Greenland, the <a href="/wiki/Bishop_of_Greenland" title="Bishop of Greenland">Bishop of Greenland</a> <a href="/wiki/Sofie_Petersen" title="Sofie Petersen">Sofie Petersen</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[116]</a></sup> estimates that 85% of the Greenlandic population are members of her congregation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[117]</a></sup> The Church of Denmark is the <a href="/wiki/State_religion" title="State religion">established church</a> through the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Denmark" title="Constitution of Denmark">Constitution of Denmark</a>:\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303468">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>The Evangelical Lutheran Church shall be the Established Church of Denmark, and, as such, it shall be supported by the State.</p><div class="templatequotecite">&#8212;&#8201;<cite>Section IV of <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Denmark" title="Constitution of Denmark">Constitution of Denmark</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[118]</a></sup></cite></div>\n</blockquote>\n<p>This applies to all of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Denmark" title="Kingdom of Denmark">Kingdom of Denmark</a>, except for the <a href="/wiki/Faroe_Islands" title="Faroe Islands">Faroe Islands</a>, as the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_the_Faroe_Islands" title="Church of the Faroe Islands">Church of the Faroe Islands</a> became independent in 2007.\n</p><p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" title="Roman Catholic">Roman Catholic</a> minority is pastorally served by the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Copenhagen" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Copenhagen">Roman Catholic Diocese of Copenhagen</a>. There are still Christian missionaries on the island, but mainly from <a href="/wiki/Charismatic_Christianity" title="Charismatic Christianity">charismatic movements</a> <a href="/wiki/Proselytism" title="Proselytism">proselytizing</a> fellow Christians.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[119]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[120]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[121]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[122]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Social_issues">Social issues</span></h3>\n<p>The rate of <a href="/wiki/Suicide_in_Greenland" title="Suicide in Greenland">suicide in Greenland</a> is very high. According to a 2010 census, Greenland holds <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_suicide_rate" title="List of countries by suicide rate">the highest suicide rate in the world</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Suicide_Capital_of_the_World_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_Suicide_Capital_of_the_World-124">[123]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rising_suicide_rate_baffles_Greenland_125-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rising_suicide_rate_baffles_Greenland-125">[124]</a></sup> Other significant social issues faced by Greenland are high rates of unemployment, alcoholism, and HIV/AIDS.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[125]</a></sup> Alcohol consumption rates in Greenland reached their height in the 1980s, when it was twice as high as in Denmark, and had by 2010 fallen slightly below the average level of consumption in Denmark (which is the 12th highest in the world). But at the same time alcohol prices are much higher, meaning that consumption has a high social impact.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[126]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[127]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Greenland" title="Culture of Greenland">Culture of Greenland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Greenland" title="Music of Greenland">Music of Greenland</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nive_Nielsen_Rudolstadt_01.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3456" data-file-width="5184" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Nive_Nielsen_Rudolstadt_01.jpg/220px-Nive_Nielsen_Rudolstadt_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Nive_Nielsen_Rudolstadt_01.jpg/330px-Nive_Nielsen_Rudolstadt_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Nive_Nielsen_Rudolstadt_01.jpg/440px-Nive_Nielsen_Rudolstadt_01.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nive_Nielsen_Rudolstadt_01.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Nive_Nielsen" title="Nive Nielsen">Nive Nielsen</a>, Greenlandic singer and songwriter</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Inuk_Silis_H%C3%B8egh,_Tommi_Kainulainen_-_WOMEX_15,_Budapest,_2015.10.22_(1).JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3240" data-file-width="4320" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Inuk_Silis_H%C3%B8egh%2C_Tommi_Kainulainen_-_WOMEX_15%2C_Budapest%2C_2015.10.22_%281%29.JPG/220px-Inuk_Silis_H%C3%B8egh%2C_Tommi_Kainulainen_-_WOMEX_15%2C_Budapest%2C_2015.10.22_%281%29.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Inuk_Silis_H%C3%B8egh%2C_Tommi_Kainulainen_-_WOMEX_15%2C_Budapest%2C_2015.10.22_%281%29.JPG/330px-Inuk_Silis_H%C3%B8egh%2C_Tommi_Kainulainen_-_WOMEX_15%2C_Budapest%2C_2015.10.22_%281%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ab/Inuk_Silis_H%C3%B8egh%2C_Tommi_Kainulainen_-_WOMEX_15%2C_Budapest%2C_2015.10.22_%281%29.JPG/440px-Inuk_Silis_H%C3%B8egh%2C_Tommi_Kainulainen_-_WOMEX_15%2C_Budapest%2C_2015.10.22_%281%29.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Inuk_Silis_H%C3%B8egh,_Tommi_Kainulainen_-_WOMEX_15,_Budapest,_2015.10.22_(1).JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Panel discussion with Greenlandic movie maker <a href="/wiki/Inuk_Silis_H%C3%B8egh" title="Inuk Silis H&#248;egh">Inuk Silis H&#248;egh</a> at the launch of his movie about groundbreaking Greenlandic band <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sume_(band)" title="Sume (band)">Sum&#233;</a>. Journalist and Sum&#233;\'s record producer Karsten Sommer is speaking.</div></div></div>\n<p>Today Greenlandic culture is a blending of traditional Inuit (<a href="/wiki/Kalaallit" title="Kalaallit">Kalaallit</a>) and Scandinavian culture. Inuit, or Kalaallit, culture has a strong artistic tradition, dating back thousands of years. The Kalaallit are known for an art form of figures called <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tupilak" title="Tupilak">tupilak</a></i> or a "spirit object." Traditional art-making practices thrive in the <i>Ammassalik</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ingo20_129-0"><a href="#cite_note-ingo20-129">[128]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sperm_whale" title="Sperm whale">Sperm whale</a> ivory remains a valued medium for carving.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[129]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Greenland also has a successful, albeit small, music culture. Some popular <a href="/wiki/Greenlandic_language" title="Greenlandic language">Greenlandic</a> bands and artists include <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sume_(band)" title="Sume (band)">Sume</a> (classic rock), <a href="/wiki/Chilly_Friday" title="Chilly Friday">Chilly Friday</a> (rock), <a href="/wiki/Nanook" title="Nanook">Nanook</a> (rock), <a href="/wiki/Siissisoq" title="Siissisoq">Siissisoq</a> (rock), <a href="/wiki/Nuuk_Posse" title="Nuuk Posse">Nuuk Posse</a> (hip hop) and <a href="/wiki/Rasmus_Lyberth" title="Rasmus Lyberth">Rasmus Lyberth</a> (folk), who performed in the <a href="/wiki/Denmark_in_the_Eurovision_Song_Contest_1979" title="Denmark in the Eurovision Song Contest 1979">Danish Eurovision Song Contest 1979</a>, performing in Greenlandic. The singer-songwriter <a href="/wiki/Simon_Lynge" title="Simon Lynge">Simon Lynge</a> is the first musical artist from Greenland to have an album released across the United Kingdom, and to perform at the UK\'s <a href="/wiki/Glastonbury_Festival" title="Glastonbury Festival">Glastonbury Festival</a>. The music culture of Greenland also includes traditional <a href="/wiki/Inuit_music" title="Inuit music">Inuit music</a>, largely revolving around singing and drums.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Greenland" title="Sport in Greenland">Sport in Greenland</a></div>\n<p>Sport is an important part of Greenlandic culture, as the population is generally quite active.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[130]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Popular sports include <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">association football</a>, <a href="/wiki/Track_and_field" title="Track and field">track and field</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Team_handball" title="Team handball">handball</a> and <a href="/wiki/Skiing" title="Skiing">skiing</a>. Handball is often referred to as the national sport,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-handball_132-0"><a href="#cite_note-handball-132">[131]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Greenland_national_handball_team" title="Greenland national handball team">Greenland\'s men\'s national team</a> was ranked among the top 20 in the world in 2001.\n</p><p>Greenland has excellent conditions for <a href="/wiki/Skiing" title="Skiing">skiing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fishing" title="Fishing">fishing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Snowboarding" title="Snowboarding">snowboarding</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ice_climbing" title="Ice climbing">ice climbing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rock_climbing" title="Rock climbing">rock climbing</a>, although <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mountain_climbing" title="Mountain climbing">mountain climbing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hiking" title="Hiking">hiking</a> are preferred by the general public. Although the country\'s environment is generally ill-suited for golf, there are nevertheless golf courses on the island.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span></h2>\n<div
